Current Commentary

Trends in Anglo-Japanese Relations 17

— Ji

Several years ago, international affairs analysts shared a common observation that the conflict between the United Kingdom and the United States was the fundamental conflict of imperialism. Anti-capitalist political commentators viewed it that way, and so did capitalist political commentators.

This situation has undergone a significant change. In the past year or two, the conflict between the United Kingdom and Japan seems to have become more serious than the conflict between the United Kingdom and the United States. The contradiction of interests in the Far East, the South Pacific (including Siam, the Malay Peninsula, the Dutch East Indies, and New Zealand), the rapid growth of Japanese economic power, and the conflict between the United Kingdom and Japan in the cotton and wool industries in India and Australia all indicate that the opposition between the United Kingdom and Japan in the commodity market is becoming increasingly tense. In the Americas, the commercial competition between the United Kingdom and Japan in Argentina, Brazil, and the British dominion of Canada is also constantly developing. Japanese commodity power is not only extending into the United Kingdom's European colonies and dominions, but also the volume of Japanese commodity exports in Northern Europe is increasing day by day. While other countries are worrying about the shrinking of foreign trade, Japan is boasting about "trade prosperity" and "Japanese commodities active in the world."

In recent years, Anglo-Japanese relations have progressed in an unbalanced state. However, due to the traditional friendship of the past, Japan still has lingering feelings for the United Kingdom. The United Kingdom also seems to want to coordinate with Japan, progressing from a compromise on Far Eastern issues to a compromise on the entire Asia and the world.

Facts have proven that this is a dream. Japan has announced its withdrawal from the naval conference. Japan has declared its opposition to Anglo-Japanese cooperation. Japan has publicly proposed conditions for opening up the United Kingdom's market in the East, considering this to be a prerequisite for maintaining the United Kingdom's practical benefits in North China and conducting direct negotiations between the United Kingdom and Japan. Due to these various events, the United Kingdom has had to change its attitude and actively promote its policies towards China independently.

Since last winter, the UK-Japan relationship, in terms of financial investment, trade, and even politics, has been progressing under a serious atmosphere. This is an undeniable fact, and the rapprochement between the United Kingdom and the Soviet Union is occurring under this circumstance.

The rapprochement between the United Kingdom and the Soviet Union and the United Kingdom's active advancement in the Far East are major challenges in Hirota's diplomatic process of East Asian monopolization. "With the vastness and complexity of the Far Eastern territories, Japan will encounter infinite difficulties if it wants to completely control it." This is an optimistic remark made by U.S. Senator Borah on the Far East issue. This statement is sufficient to explain the reality of international relations in the Far East.

Therefore, how to adjust relations with the United Kingdom is the mechanism of Hirota's so-called proactive and independent diplomacy. Japan hopes that the United Kingdom can engage in adjusting Anglo-Japanese relations on the premise of respecting Japan's principle of monopolizing East Asia. However, is this possible? Our answer is definitely impossible, unless the "red menace" would endanger the United Kingdom's fundamental power in the East.

Recently, Japanese news agencies have been trying their best to spread news of a compromise being reached between the United Kingdom and Japan. At the same time, they are also spreading news that British Ambassador to China, Sir Hughe Knatchbull-Hugessen, will visit Japan on his way home and hold informal Anglo-Japanese meetings with Japanese authorities to exchange views on the Far East issue. Although this news has not yet been fully confirmed, how Japan's policy toward the United Kingdom will change in the future is worth our attention because its influence will not only affect China but also the entire world.

Renewed Conflict Between Japanese and Russian Troops Near Changlingzi 18

Both Sides Opened Fire for Several Hours

Japanese Troops Abandoned Two Corpses and Retreat

Moscow, Today, Around 10:00 AM, Borike time, seven armed Japanese soldiers, in the Huichun area near the borders of the Soviet Union, Manchuria, and Korea, crossed from Manchuria into Soviet territory, penetrating 250 meters inside the border. They opened fire on a Soviet patrol team (comprised of five border guards) 300 meters from the border. The two sides clashed for half an hour, resulting in the Japanese troops being forced to retreat, abandoning the corpses of one Japanese officer and one soldier within Soviet territory. At 3:50 PM, 50 to 60 Japanese soldiers crossed the border again, carrying several light and heavy machine guns, and invaded 250 meters from the same area near the No. 8 boundary marker, occupying the high ground. They fired rifles and machine guns at Soviet border guards and a distant outpost. The border guards fought back valiantly, and the Japanese troops were forced to retreat back into Manchurian territory in the evening. Both sides suffered casualties. According to TASS news, Moscow received a report of the Japanese invasion of the Soviet border, and the Soviet Ambassador to Tokyo immediately protested to the Japanese government, demanding a strict investigation into the actions of the Japanese military authorities, punishment of those responsible, and reserving the Soviet Union's right to claim compensation for losses. (TASS dispatch, 26th)

Tokyo, The Ministry of the Army announced that at 9:00 AM on March 25th, in the territory of "Manchukuo" four li southeast of Huichun, near Changlingzi on the Russo-Manchurian border, nine Japanese soldiers, including officers, were reconnoitering the terrain when Russian soldiers suddenly opened fire illegally. The Japanese troops, for self-defense, immediately returned fire but, fearing an escalation of the situation, retreated 1,000 meters. However, the Russian troops continued to fire, relentlessly pursuing and attacking, causing several Japanese soldiers, including officers, to be wounded. The Japanese army urgently dispatched several dozen troops as reinforcements. This unit, together with the border guards, remained on alert. At 4:40 PM, the Russian troops resumed heavy fire with a strong force, and the Japanese and Manchurian troops had no choice but to return fire. The fighting ceased at night, and the Russian troops retreated north of Changlingzi. The Japanese troops also withdrew from the front lines, concentrating in the rear. Two Japanese officers, one non-commissioned officer, and five soldiers, as well as three Manchurian soldiers, were wounded. (Dentsu dispatch, 26th)

Tokyo, Foreign Minister Hirota met with Soviet Ambassador to Japan, Yurenev, at 3:00 PM on the 26th regarding the Changlingzi incident. The Foreign Ministry authorities released the following information regarding the content of the meeting: Foreign Minister Hirota received a detailed report from local officials regarding the Changlingzi incident on the morning of the 26th. He immediately telegraphed Ambassador Ota in the Soviet Union, instructing him to lodge a serious protest with the Soviet government. At 3:00 PM on the same day, he met with Soviet Ambassador Yurenev at the Prime Minister's residence, stating that the Soviet border patrol had opened fire on Japanese officers who were observing near the border without any other intention, without issuing any prior warning. Such reckless behavior should be seriously protested, and the Soviet side should promptly eliminate the atmosphere of unrest in the area. (Domei dispatch, 26th)

Harbin, At approximately 5:00 PM on the 25th of this month, a unit of Japanese troops clashed with border guards of Outer Mongolia near Hailar, resulting in a fierce battle for over an hour. One Japanese scout was killed. The number of Mongolian casualties is unknown. (Chinese United Press dispatch, 26th)

Minister of the Army Terauchi Explains Inside Story of Tokyo Incident 19

Many Parties Responded After the Incident

Fortunately, Authorities Dealt With it in Time to Prevent Escalation

Efforts to Prevent Undermining of People's Military Service Obligations

Tokyo, At a meeting of local governors at 1:00 PM on the 26th, Minister of the Army Terauchi explained the details of the February 26th incident as follows:

Slander against the military and anti-military movements, now accompanied by ominous events carried out by a few officers colluding with external extremist elements, are a violation of the duties of soldiers, disrupting military discipline, and leaving a stain on the glorious history of the nation. Such behavior cannot be tolerated, and the responsibility must be borne by the entire military. There are those who falsely accuse the military, claiming there are still many bad elements within, and even spreading rumors that this incident had the tacit understanding of some military leaders. Such people are intentionally damaging the reputation of the military, causing its authority to be lost, and plotting the separation of the military and the people through anti-national, anti-military movements. We sincerely hope to prevent such anti-military movements early and achieve unity between the military and the people.

The relationship between the incident and external forces; the scope of the current incident is not limited to the military, but seems to have reached various levels outside the military, with a considerable number of people involved. These people colluded with a section of people within the military, leading to the incident. Furthermore, after the incident, there were many who acted rashly in response. Fortunately, the authorities dealt with it promptly, preventing its escalation. In the future, we must eliminate these bad elements and eradicate the root of the disaster. The road ahead is long, and I hope everyone will continue to work hard.

Crack down on strange documents; recently, there has been a significant increase in strange documents, which is very regrettable. The occurrence of the current incident, and the social unrest after it, are undoubtedly directly related to these strange documents. For the benefit of protecting the country and the national army, thoroughly cracking down on strange documents is an urgent matter at present.

Prevent the undermining of the public's sense of military service obligation; in the current incident, the general soldiers who obeyed the orders of their superiors and joined the rebel army are truly pitiful, and the military, which failed to prevent it beforehand, also bears significant responsibility. These soldiers are currently being tried by the judicial authorities, and the determination of responsibility for those who fundamentally obeyed orders will be clarified with a cautious attitude, so as not to leave trouble for the future. If the current incident leads to an undermining of the sense of military service obligation, or a decrease in the number of people supporting the military, then the national defense will be truly worrying. (Domei dispatch, 26th)

Japan Sets Meeting of Division Commanders for the 7th of Next Month 20

To Convey Purge Policy

Tokyo, In light of the internal and external situation, Minister of the Army Terauchi, not allowing any delay in implementing the military purge, has set the meeting of all army commanders and division commanders for the 7th of next month to communicate the purge policy thoroughly as scheduled. Furthermore, at the meeting of local governors on the 26th, personnel were dispatched to explain the truth of the February 26th incident and the basis of the military purge, hoping for the assistance of local officials and civilians. After the urgent problems within and outside the army that need to be resolved come to a conclusion, the Minister of the Army will, with a significant resolution, investigate the social, economic, and political causes of the February 26th incident, tracing back to its roots and eradicating the causes of the disaster. After Generals Umezu, Nishio, and Isoya assume their positions, the Minister of the Army will convene a meeting of the army leadership to discuss specific policies. (Domei dispatch, 26th)

They immediately opened fire, engaging in a fierce battle for a long time. Nearby Japanese troops, hearing the news, rushed to the scene, and the Revolutionary Army began to retreat. Japan's Invasion of Manchuria Claims 170,000 Lives 26

Announced by the Ministry of the Army

According to the Nagoya Shimbun, a survey by the Ministry of the Army reveals that since the Manchurian Incident, up to the end of last year, the number of casualties has reached 171,398, including 2,871 in Showa Year 6 (1931), 31,738 in Year 7 (1932), 42,149 in Year 8 (1933), 34,874 in Year 9 (1934), and 54,766 in Year 10 (1935). Among them, 2,884 died in battle, 392 died from injuries, 702 died from illness, 222 died from other causes, 8,034 were wounded in battle, 2,588 suffered frostbite, 137,647 fell ill, and 19,855 suffered external injuries. Even now, there is still an average of two to three deaths and thirty to thirty-five injuries per day. This is truly a great sacrifice that Japan has suffered in Manchuria.

Ancient Chinese Tapestries and Carpets Exhibited in France 27

President of the Academy of Fine Arts Presides Over Ceremony

Paris, The exhibition of ancient Chinese tapestries and carpets opened today at the French National Gobelins Tapestry Factory, presided over by the Minister of Education, Gnou, and the President of the Academy of Fine Arts. The exhibition showcased a dazzling array of works from the 6th to 19th centuries, inspiring sighs of wonder. According to the Director of the Factory, Marnier, speaking to our reporter, "For two years, we have collected tapestries and carpets from various countries in the Near East, as well as from the Peruvian, Egyptian, and Coptic peoples of America, and held separate exhibitions. This time, we will collect extensively from various countries in the Far East, particularly China, tapestries, kesi, and wool and silk carpets from the 10th century onwards to study their development. This will surely be welcomed by those generally concerned with Chinese art. We are also honored that the National Louvre Museum, the Museum of Fine Arts and History in Brussels, Belgium, the Guimet Museum, and many collectors in France and abroad, particularly Mr. Villonet of Lausanne (known at the time for his research on Chinese symbolism and ancient Far Eastern textiles), have generously lent their treasured masterpieces for display, adding much luster. What is displayed this time are primarily ancient Chinese kesi masterpieces, whose ingenuity is breathtaking and worthy of admiration, and which are all able to preserve the inherent spirit of the Chinese nation. This is in harmony with the Gothic tapestries hanging in ancient French churches. There are also Japanese "Nishiki tapestries," which are also exquisitely beautiful, on par with Chinese kesi. As for modern Chinese silk tapestries imitating the ancients, their production techniques are comparable to 'kesi.' In addition, there are also Chinese embroidery, Tibetan textiles, and Chinese carpets, among which Chinese carpets were only introduced to France in the mid-19th century, so our research on them is not yet very thorough. As for the arrangement of this exhibition, it is arranged sequentially according to the system and age of various products for easy viewing," he said. (Havas dispatch, 26th)

British and Japanese Silk Industry Competition 28

London, The British and Irish Silk Weaving Industry Association held its spring banquet here last night, where President Farrell delivered a speech, warning about the competition from Japanese silk products in the British market. He said that if the government does not raise tariffs on Japanese goods in a timely manner, the threat to the British silk weaving industry will inevitably be impossible to eliminate, and also said, "The government should pay attention to the production of certain items within the country that are originally necessities for national defense at all times. Therefore, in the event of war, the government must reorganize various industries, and the silk weaving industry is actually in an important position. However, if various government departments continue to order Japanese goods, then the national defense plan will inevitably be impossible to complete. The Association has previously strongly advocated that when King Edward VIII holds his coronation ceremony in the future, all silk products used should be domestic goods as much as possible. In addition, Sir Joseph, president of the Federation of Industries, also delivered a speech, saying that Japan's exports are increasing daily, and its means of competing with British goods are unscrupulous, such as imitating the styles of British goods and counterfeiting British trademarks. (Havas dispatch, 26th)

German-Polish Negotiations on Transportation Issues 29

Warsaw, German trains passing through the Polish Corridor are in debt, which has not yet been paid off (totalling approximately 185,000,000 francs). Therefore, the Polish government, starting from February 7th of this year, ordered the suspension of all trains to Berlin. The two countries immediately entered into negotiations to find a solution. The German government has recently instructed its ambassador to Poland, Moltke, to handle the case with full authority. After receiving the order, Moltke immediately visited Polish Prime Minister Gutschelkowski to discuss the matter. According to the semi-official Berlin German News Agency, an agreement is expected to be reached soon. (Havas dispatch, 26th)

Britain, America, and France Sign Naval Treaty 30

Pacific Defense Augmentation Issue - Britain, America, and Japan Conduct Negotiations

London, The new Anglo-American-French London Naval Treaty was formally signed at the naval conference at St. James's Palace this afternoon. Signatories included American representatives Davis and Stanley, French representatives Corbin and Robert, and British representatives Eden and Monsell. Representatives of the British Empire's self-governing dominions and India, with the exception of South Phi and the South Irish Free State, also signed in place of the soon-to-expire Washington Treaty, effective from December 31st for a period of six years. (Reuters dispatch, 25th)

London, British representative Eden and American representative Davis exchanged letters after the signing, containing the agreement reached during the talks between the British and American delegations. In his letter, Davis declared that there should be no naval construction competition between Britain and America, and that the principle of equality between the British and American navies would remain unchanged. Eden's letter acknowledged this agreement, stating that there should be no naval construction competition between Britain and America, and that Britain fully agreed that neither party should question the other's right to maintain mutual equality in any type of warship, and further stated that Britain had never taken into consideration the naval power of the United States when estimating its naval needs. (Reuters dispatch, 26th)

Washington, Here, it is believed that the exchange of official documents between US Envoy Davis and British Foreign Secretary Eden re-establishing the British-American naval balance is a continuation of the 1930 naval conference policy and a guarantee that a naval construction competition will not occur between Britain and America. It is said that the exchange of documents between the two countries proves that the positions of the two countries aim to avoid giving rise to the impression that an alliance has been formed between Britain and America. Officials here state that there is no meaning of an alliance, let alone anything else. (National Telegraph dispatch, 25th)

Washington, After the signing of the Anglo-American-French naval treaty, there was a general welcome here. Secretary of State Hull, in the name of President Roosevelt and himself, sent a telegram to the US Chief Representative Davis, extending his congratulations. The authorities concerned regretted that quantitative restrictions could not be established, fearing that the United States would have to increase naval expenditures in order to maintain its security. However, the United States wishes to prevent naval competition, and the construction program will be limited to destroyers and submarines to reach the numbers stipulated in the 1930 London Naval Treaty. As for other types of ships that have exceeded their service life, they will be replaced. For example, the battleships "Arkansas" and "New York", whose service lives expired in 1932 and 1934 respectively, the Navy Department will begin constructing two new ships this year to replace them. If the principle of quantitative restriction is considered, the US naval policy will still maintain a ratio of 5 to 3 with Japan and maintain parity with Britain. The British government's White Paper on National Defense Plans, published at the beginning of this month, stipulates the addition of 20 light cruisers to reach a number of 70. The US Navy Department also intends to add several warships to maintain parity, but the type of warship to be built has not yet been decided. In addition, members of Congress, due to the fact that Japan has established naval bases on the mandated islands in the Pacific, have also proposed deploying defenses on the US-owned islands in the Pacific. However, officials are unwilling to express their views, and this issue will inevitably be mentioned when Congress discusses the approval of the naval treaty in the future. (Havas dispatch, 25th)

London, In view of the fact that Article 19 of the Washington Treaty will no longer be effectively enforced, Britain is building defensive works and naval bases in the Far East. Japan has inquired of Britain about its intentions in this regard. Britain, America, and Japan are currently discussing this matter through diplomatic channels, and Japan has not yet given a final reply. (Reuters dispatch, 25th)

London Naval Plenary Session 31

London, The naval conference held a plenary session at 4:15 PM today in the Queen Anne Room of St. James's Palace, where Britain, France, and the United States signed the naval treaty. The original chairman was British Foreign Secretary Eden, but because Eden did not arrive at the venue until the signing, Lord Monsell, the British Secretary of the Admiralty, temporarily chaired the session. The chairman spoke first, followed by American Chief Representative Davis, and then the signing ceremony was held. After the ceremony, French Chief Representative Ambassador Corbin, Indian representative Boardlow, and Italian Chief Representative Ambassador Grandi delivered speeches in succession. The meeting adjourned at 5:17 PM. (Havas dispatch, 25th)

London, At today's meeting, in addition to Italy not signing the treaty, the South Irish Free State and the South African Federation also did not sign. South Ireland had separate political reasons, believing that the naval treaty could have a dangerous impact on the state's policies. The South African Federation, on the other hand, said that it has never had a navy from the beginning. Japan sent two observers to attend the ceremony, one being Fujinami, Counselor of the Japanese Embassy in Britain, and the other being Navy Captain Fujita, but neither spoke. (Havas dispatch, 25th)

British Representative Speech: Hope Japan and Italy will Participate 32

London, British Navy Minister Monsell spoke after the signing ceremony, hoping that Italy and Japan would join the treaty in the future, and welcoming Japan's promise that it does not intend to take any action that would promote future naval construction competition. He also said that the signatories of the Washington Treaty, including Japan, will soon sign a draft treaty stipulating the use of warships in wartime, which he considered a good sign. US representative Davis said that while this new treaty did not satisfy the best hopes, it retained many values of the old treaty and contained important new clauses. The United States is willing to reduce the size of warships, but since the United States began building warships, it has only been 15 years, and it must wait until the United States has experience with one or more new types of warships before it can determine the extent to which the tonnage of warships can be reduced. The US representative also said that if the number of warships increases, even if the tonnage of each ship is reduced, it will not promote disarmament. Freedom regarding the number of ships is something we use improperly, and this largely depends on the goodwill of the naval countries to abide by the spirit and letter of the new treaty. (Reuters dispatch, 25th)

US Representative Speech: Naval Competition Can Be Avoided 33

London, Davis, the chief representative of the United States at the London Naval Conference, today signed the Anglo-French-American naval treaty on behalf of President Roosevelt and narrated the United States' policy and opinions on naval disarmament and expressed optimistic hopes for the opportunity to reduce armaments in the world. Mr. Davis said that the United States was very pleased to sign this treaty, "Which can help implement some of the basic principles of naval disarmament, and with the goodwill of the naval countries, it can prevent naval competition after the expiration of the Washington and London treaties." Mr. Davis solemnly stated that the United States regretted that this treaty could not stipulate quantitative reductions and limitations on naval strength, because the attitude of the United States has not changed since 1921, and it still believes that the only way to stabilize naval relations between countries is through reduction. However, the United States has not abandoned the hope of future quantitative restrictions, "If we consider the world situation at the opening of the meeting and the various crises after the opening, it can be seen that its success was indeed unexpected. Moreover, military expansion is actually a response to international instability and mutual suspicion. Therefore, in this environment, it is impossible to reduce armaments on a large scale." Mr. Davis also said that the danger of competing to build new types of warships is actually greater than competition in numbers, because new things are enough to arouse mutual suspicion, and building new types of warships to make existing warships obsolete is the most wasteful competition. Therefore, quantitative restrictions are most valuable. This concluded treaty can show the wisdom of the representatives of Britain, the United States, France, and Italy in working hard to reach an agreement after the Japanese representatives withdrew from the meeting. There are many clauses in the treaty that can help countries avoid unnecessary construction. The most important is that each signatory country must notify each other of its construction plans in advance, and the strict system of exchanging information with each other can avoid suspicion and prevent mutual competition. "We believe that this will regulate a country's construction program without being seen as an action that harms other countries." Mr. Davis went on to say that the United States has allowed the suspension of the construction of 10,000-ton cruisers for six years to show that the United States is willing to limit naval construction at any time. However, if an agreement is reached on this point, it must be conditional on not excessively increasing the number of smaller cruisers, and after mutual notification and consultation, this agreement can also be terminated. The reason why the United States cannot allow the reduction of the tonnage of battleships to below 35,000 tons is because the United States has not built this type of warship for fifteen years, so it must build one or two more before it can be sure of the tonnage of this type of warship can be reduced. However, it is hoped that this issue will be discussed again in the future. As for whether quantitative restrictions can ultimately solve naval competition, it is impossible to know at present, but if there is a broader treaty in the future, it can be used as a transition, and international understanding will not be destroyed. (National Telegraph dispatch, 26th)

Judicial Yuan Interprets Negotiable Instruments Law Nanjing

The Judicial Yuan interprets the ambiguities in the Negotiable Instruments Law as follows: If a bill of exchange issued by B with C as the payee has been endorsed to A in blank by C, and then transferred by A to D, then when D exercises the right of recourse against B according to law, B shall not claim that it is not responsible to D, nor may it deny the exercise of the right of recourse on the grounds that C has a letter of exchange. (Central News Agency dispatch on the 26th)

Guangdong Province

Improving Tobacco Production in Guangdong

Establishing Tobacco Trial Field in Nanxiong County

Providing Low-Interest Loans to Tobacco Farmers for Planting

Guangzhou Correspondence: Guangdong Province has recently implemented a special tobacco trade and is trying to develop local tobacco cultivation to resist the encroachment of imported cigarettes. According to a survey, the total annual output of local tobacco leaves in Guangdong Province is 429,193 dan (100 catties per dan). Of this, 63,100 dan are exported and more than 366,000 dan are sold domestically. The annual sales value is more than 8,635,000 yuan. In this province alone, about 108,500 dan of flue-cured tobacco are sold. If improved further, local tobacco can easily regain the market share of imported cigarettes, saving a considerable amount of money that flows overseas each year. The largest production areas of local tobacco in the province are Nanxiong in northern Guangdong. Since the authorities implemented the local tobacco monopoly, the Guangdong-Guangxi-Fujian Unified Tax Bureau has appointed a resident Nanxiong specialist manager to set up a monopoly office in Nanxiong City and provide low-interest loans to tobacco farmers in accordance with regulations, so that tobacco farmers can have capital to engage in planting. The loan methods are as follows:

1. In order to promote the improvement of tobacco production by farmers, the Tobacco Trial Field has specially formulated these methods for compliance.

2. The occupational scope of the loan for tobacco planting by this field is temporarily limited to a certain area.

3. All farmers who apply to this field for a loan to plant tobacco must fill out an application form in accordance with these methods and submit it to this field for review.

4. Farmers who apply for a loan to plant tobacco must have a guarantee from the Nanxiong Tobacco Leaf Sales Cooperative or a reputable store before they can get the loan.

5. The loan amount is temporarily set at two dan of fertilizer per mu (the price of this fertilizer is negotiated with the fertilizer manufacturer at ten yuan per dan, including freight), and a certain amount of tobacco seeds are provided free of charge. After the harvest, the tobacco leaves will be returned, and the value of the tobacco leaves will be agreed upon by this field and the borrower at the time of signing the contract.

6. Farmers who apply for a loan to plant tobacco must sign a loan contract with this field in person when the loan is approved.

7. Once the tobacco leaves are harvested, tobacco farmers who have taken out a loan to plant tobacco must send them to this field's improved curing room to dry and hand them over to this field as repayment of the loan. The calculation is based on the agreed value in the contract. Any surplus will be returned and any deficiency will be recovered.

8. All curing labor, materials and expenses shall be borne by this field.

9. Tobacco farmers who have taken out a loan to plant tobacco must plant at least half of the planted area with the tobacco seeds provided by this field. The rest can be freely planted with local tobacco leaves.

10. The tobacco seeds planted by tobacco farmers who have taken out a loan shall be supervised and managed by this field and shall not be freely sold. The planting methods must also be subject to the instructions of this field. If there is any deliberate violation, this field may revoke its contract at any time and recover all outstanding payments.

11. The original curing room of tobacco farmers who have taken out a loan must be supervised by this field for reconstruction. The reconstruction and equipment costs shall be provided by this field. The amount loaned shall be repaid to this field by the borrower starting from the settlement year.

12. If the tobacco farmers who have taken out a loan do not continue to renew the contract in the settlement year, the curing room and equipment built by this field may be dismantled by this field, or the farmer may prepare funds to take over.

13. If there are any matters not covered in these methods, they shall be submitted by this field to the competent authority for approval and addition or deletion.

The Nanxiong Tobacco Trial Field is jointly operated by the Department of Construction, the Bureau of Agriculture and Forestry, and the Nanxiong County Government. The field is located in Nanxiong County and has an area of 30 mu. All trial tobacco varieties, cultivation methods, tobacco production methods, and breeding of superior tobacco seeds are implemented in the field. (March 20)

Page 8

Smuggling Remains Rampant After Tianjin Customs and Railways Implement Anti-Smuggling Measures

Japanese Consul in Tianjin Lodges Protest

Tianjin Correspondence: After the Tianjin Customs and the Beining Railway established six anti-smuggling measures and began implementing them on the 21st, the Customs, for the convenience of handling affairs, established a Customs Inspection Office for Railway Goods at No. 181 Xinda Road, Hebei, and assigned two foreign customs officers to be stationed there permanently to handle the procedures for inspecting declaration forms. In addition, four customs officers were stationed at each of the East and West Main Stations to collect tax bills from freight owners day and night and on holidays. The goods that are required to be declared for inspection include rayon, cigarette paper, seafood, alcoholic beverages (whiskey, champagne, etc.), radio equipment, fur, velvet, medicines, car tires, rickshaw tires, porcelain, soap, and various colors of cloth, totaling dozens of types. According to this list of goods, the railway will refuse to load any freight that the owner requests the railway to transport without going through customs inspection procedures. However, since the implementation of the measures, few people have declared for inspection. Goods transshipped to other places, under the armed protection of Japanese and Korean ronin, are loaded onto large cars and no longer take the railway. Instead, they display the flag of the Japan International Transportation Company and travel south along the Jinpu Railway. Those transported to the Huainan area are loaded onto trains between Jinghai and Cangxian and transported to that area. Those transported to Gaoyang and Qingyuan in southern Hebei are sent by car. Every time smuggled goods are transported out of Tianjin, when passing through the Da Yingmen thoroughfare, the ronin hold a gun in their hands, glare angrily, and rush past the inspection post. Therefore, smuggling is rampant and has not been affected by the implementation of the new anti-smuggling law. As for those smuggled from eastern Hebei, because the puppet government has recently set up tax checkpoints along the ports of Changli, collecting extremely low tariffs, the ronin hold the tax bills and load the goods onto trains to Tianjin for public unloading. When customs officials inquire, they show the puppet tax bills as proof that the tax has been paid, and customs officers cannot interfere too much, otherwise disaster will strike. Therefore, the smuggling of goods from eastern Hebei has not been affected by the new anti-smuggling law. Regarding the assistance of the Jinpu Railway in anti-smuggling, the Tianjin Customs sent the method established with the Beining Railway to the Tianjin Office of the Jinpu Railway, requesting assistance as usual. The office forwarded the request to the head office, and on the 22nd, it received a reply by telegram approving it. On the 23rd, it also followed the request of the Customs and refused to load foreign goods that had not been declared for inspection and did not have a declaration form. However, this rule is limited to the East and West Main Stations in Tianjin, and the efforts of the customs officials themselves at each station along the line will determine the outcome. Lin Shize, the superintendent of the Tianjin Customs, returned to Tianjin from Peiping on the 22nd. Regarding the diplomatic problems caused by the Customs and the Railway Bureau's anti-smuggling efforts, he assisted Chen Zhongfu and Chen Juesheng in resolving the diplomatic disputes. According to him, the anti-smuggling measures of the Tianjin Customs and the Railway Bureau are not thorough. In eastern Hebei, the fundamental problem lies in the abolition of the puppet regime and our problem. It is currently difficult to figure out how to combat smuggling. Since the smuggling of foreign goods has not been successfully stopped, and there are fears of causing misunderstandings abroad, it is more important to remove unexpected difficulties than to combat smuggling. He said that if difficulties are removed, anti-smuggling can be carried out as desired. His words show that there are still many thorns on the road ahead. As for the Japanese side, they believe that the Tianjin Customs and the Beining Railway's assistance in anti-smuggling hinders the sales of Japanese goods, and they also point out that the Beining Railway Bureau is deliberately discriminating against Japanese goods and helping the Customs in its investigations. On the 21st, Kawayue, the Japanese consul general in Tianjin, sent the commercial consul Nishida to visit Chen Juesheng, the director of the Beining Railway Bureau, to lodge a verbal protest. Chen told him that the Customs was in charge of this matter, and the Beining Railway only provided assistance within the scope of its capabilities and had no intention of discriminating against Japanese goods. If the procedures for Japanese goods were complete, they could be loaded and transported at any time. Nishida did not find the reply satisfactory and visited Xu Liya, the chief of the Tianjin Customs, that afternoon, making the same statement. Chen Zhongfu and Chen Juesheng visited the Japanese consul together on the 23rd to explain the misunderstanding, and the Japanese side's anger began to subside. The Beining Railway also replied to the Japanese consulate in writing on the same day. According to observations, the Japanese ronin's smuggling to and from Japan has not been affected, and the Customs does not dare to enforce the law for fear of unexpected changes. The Japanese protest is only a necessary expression and may not be expanded. (23rd)

Guangzhou Busts Counterfeit Foreign Currency Agency

200,000 Yuan in Counterfeit HSBC Banknotes Seized

Coining Machine and Principal Culprit Captured Separately

Guangzhou Correspondence: Guangzhou and Hong Kong have close commercial relations, and trade between Chinese and foreign merchants is flourishing. Moreover, due to the proximity of the locations, foreign currency has always circulated in the interior of Guangdong Province, with British HSBC banknotes flowing into the interior the most, occupying an important position in the financial sector of Guangdong Province. Since HSBC banknotes are mixed with domestic legal tender on the market, criminals often counterfeit HSBC banknotes and mix them on the market in order to make huge profits. A few years ago, the case of Cui Mingzhou counterfeiting HSBC banknotes in Henan, Guangzhou caused a sensation. Unexpectedly, after Cui was executed, the communists dared to imitate his old tricks and manufacture counterfeit HSBC banknotes. Recently, counterfeit HSBC banknotes have been discovered on the market again. Upon receiving the report, the authorities secretly dispatched detectives to investigate closely. After three months of investigations, the Criminal Investigation Team of the Guangdong Military Police Headquarters has found clues and learned that there are three counterfeit currency agencies: one is Zhang Meicheng's store at No. 18 Datang Street, Xichan Branch, Xiguan, Guangzhou, one is a residence on Zilai Street, Section 3, Panyu, Henan, and one is Jianzao Company at No. 10 Huanan Heng Street, Changshou Branch, Xiguan. The Jianwei Company is the central agency. Recently, due to the widespread deployment of police officers, the central agency moved to Guiyuan Residence at No. 11 Yaohua Lane. Chen Bingsheng, the captain of the Criminal Investigation Team of the Military Police Department, led detectives to search the locations on the morning of the 19th of the month. First, they went to the Wei Jian 造厂 factory and seized a set of printing plates for manufacturing counterfeit HSBC banknotes, a bottle of chemicals, and more than 1,000 yuan of counterfeit HSBC banknotes with a face value of 100 yuan. They immediately arrested four shop employees, Tan Lun, Tan Weizhi, Tan Weimin, and Tan Weichang, at the factory. Then, they sent another team to search No. 11 Yaohua Lane and arrested the principal culprit, Tan Chang. They also found a large and small counterfeit currency manufacturing machine in the basement of the house, and a total of 200,000 yuan of counterfeit HSBC banknotes (with a face value of 100 yuan). Finally, they arrested the store owner, Zhang Jinpei, at No. 18 Datang Street, who was said to be closely related to the case, and found a counterfeit HSBC 100-yuan note, a 50-yuan note, and three 10-yuan notes in Zhang's house, and sent them all to the county for investigation. The principal culprit, Tan Chang, was sent to the Ministry for interrogation. He confessed to manufacturing counterfeit HSBC banknotes. It is said that Tan studied abroad, is fluent in European and American languages, and is skilled in mechanics. The counterfeit currency manufacturing machine that was seized was made by him. There is no noise during printing, so it is not easy for outsiders to hear. The manufactured counterfeit currency is not much different from the real one. Upon closer inspection, the colors are the same, but the watermark of the counterfeit one is not obvious. Ordinary people do not notice the flaws. It is also said that Tan was an assistant to Cui Mingzhou, the perpetrator of the counterfeit foreign currency case a few years ago. After Cui's death, Tan resumed his old business and was only busted now. (March 21)

French Representative's Speech: Practical Effects are Better Than Nothing 35

London - The chief French representative, Mr. Corbin, delivered a speech saying, "The French government is very pleased to sign the Second London Naval Treaty (the First London Naval Treaty was only signed by England, the United States, and Japan, and France and Italy did not participate). Since the opening of the naval conference, the difficulties encountered have been numerous. Although the new treaty has now been established, its scope is not as broad as we had expected. In addition, the 1922 Washington Naval Treaty was signed by England, France, the United States, Italy, and Japan, but now only three countries have signed the new one. All these shortcomings are enough to expose the difficulties we have encountered. The system of quantitative restrictions for a long period no longer exists, and the French delegation does not regret this, because the results obtained from the implementation of this method for fourteen years have only proved its arbitrary nature and made all countries feel unhappy. Regarding qualitative restrictions, we hope that our original intention was not too extravagant, but that we would achieve tangible results. Unfortunately, the results obtained have not fully met our expectations. However, we also know that the current qualitative restriction method, even if it has little practical effect, is better than nothing. Therefore, we still accept the huge tonnage figures for battleships. Fortunately, the naval treaty contains a clause stipulating that these figures can be reconsidered and reduced by the countries concerned in 1940, which is what France is comforted by. In addition, the caliber of battleship guns has been reduced from 16 inches to 14 inches, which is also a tangible progress. As for the tonnage of Class A cruisers, France originally advocated reducing it. Later, because the new naval treaty stipulates that countries may not build 10,000-ton cruisers during the effective period of the treaty, France has also accepted it. It is deeply hoped that countries will not build such warships before the new naval treaty is ratified. In addition, the new naval treaty also includes a clause, that is, it is hoped that the naval armaments of various countries will be reduced in the future. This is what the French representatives expect. We believe that if all countries can gradually expand the exchange of information methods stipulated in the new naval treaty, the result of reducing naval armaments can be achieved quickly. In short, the signing of the naval treaty this time is the first voice in implementing the various principles contained in the League of Nations Covenant. From now on, if no unexpected events occur regarding the shipbuilding issue, so that the mutual trust between naval countries can be restored, it will be even more hopeful," he said. (Havas News Agency, 25th)

Key Points of the Naval Treaty 37

London - The full text of the naval treaty between England, France, and the United States is divided into five parts, plus two annexes. The main points of the treaty are summarized as follows:

Part 1: Definitions of ship types. The tonnage and ship types of various ships, whether sailing on the surface or underwater, are explained. Surface warships are divided into the following types: (A) 10,000 tons or more are battleships; (B) up to 8,000 tons are cruisers; (C) all those equipped with special decks for aircraft to take off and land are aircraft carriers; (D) light warships, such as destroyers; (E) small warships, such as coastal defense shallow-water ships; (F) auxiliary ships and scout ships.

Part 2: Qualitative restriction methods, including: (A) Battleship tonnage is limited to 35,000 tons, but it is forbidden to build warships above 8,000 tons and below 17,000 tons. The caliber of battleship guns is limited to 254 mm to 356 mm (i.e., 10 inches to 14 inches); (B) Aircraft carrier tonnage is limited to 23,000 tons, and the caliber of guns is limited to 155 mm (i.e., 6 and 1/12 inches) and may not exceed ten; (C) Submarine tonnage is limited to 2,000 tons, and the caliber of guns is limited to 130 mm (i.e., 5 and 1/12 inches); (D) Cruisers with a gun caliber of 203 mm (i.e., 8 inches) (i.e., 10,000-ton Class A cruisers) are not allowed to be built while non-signatory countries do not build such warships.

Part 3: Shipbuilding procedures, advance notification, and information exchange methods. Each signatory country should notify each other of its annual shipbuilding program within the first four months of the year. Also, whenever a decision is made to build a ship, the tonnage, speed, gun caliber, and number of personnel of the new warship should be notified to other signatory countries four months before construction begins.

Part 4: So-called guarantee clauses, there are three items: (A) In the event of war; (B) When a non-signatory country does not comply with the qualitative restriction methods contained in this treaty; (C) Any change in circumstances not stipulated in items A and B. Once any of the above events occur, if one of the signatory countries wants to implement the guarantee clauses, it should notify the other signatory countries. If a compromise is not reached after three months, each signatory country may restore free action.

Part 5: Stipulates that a conference should be convened in 1940, two years before the expiration of this treaty, to discuss quantitative restriction methods. (Havas News Agency, 25th)

Recent Three Years' Export Values 56

Recent three years' statistics of major export commodity values: Raw Silk: 1933: 57,287,933; 1934: 28,755,688; 1935: 40,537,926. Tea: 1933: 34,210,037; 1934: 36,098,549; 1935: 29,624,184. Total Import and Export Values and Trade Deficit 57

Statistics of total import and export values and trade deficit: 1933: Imports: 1,345,567,188; Exports: 61,827,990; Trade Deficit: 733,739,198. 1934: Imports: 1,029,665,224; Exports: 535,214,279; Trade Deficit: 494,450,945. 1935: Imports: 919,211,322; Exports: 5,758,090,60; Trade Deficit: 343,402,262.

Foodstuffs Rank First in Imports 58

From the above figures, it can be observed that foreign imports over the years are dominated by foodstuffs. For example, the combined value of rice, wheat, and flour imported in 1935, along with the "other miscellaneous grains and flours" item listed in the customs trade book at 5,460,871, totals 135,927,318, accounting for two-fifths of the total trade deficit that year. Cotton and its products exceeded 60 million, also accounting for one-fifth of the total trade deficit that year. As for China's exports in 1935, tung oil ranked first, raw silk second, eggs and egg products third, and tea fourth. Except for tung oil exports, which increased compared to previous years, silk and tea have both declined. Comparing the 200,000 dan of raw silk exported in 1935 to the 900,000 dan in 1920, it is nearly less than a quarter. Tea exports in 1935 were 29 million yuan, compared to 88 million yuan in 1920, also only slightly more than a quarter. For thousands of years, China has been known as an agriculture-based country. Trade with advanced industrial nations involving the import of manufactured and semi-finished products is certainly to be expected, but this year, foodstuffs unexpectedly rank first among imports, accounting for the largest value of imports, while exports of agricultural raw materials are declining year by year. The trade trends and their harms are evident.

Efforts to Promote Increased Exports 59

According to the Ministry's research results, the main factor constituting the trade deficit is indeed that imports are more than exports. The adjustment measures, in addition to passively reducing unnecessary imports, should focus on actively promoting the increase of exports, which is the most urgent task at hand. The formation of China's huge trade deficit is in fact due to insufficient exports. For example, in 1933, the total value of imports reached 1,345,567,188 yuan, while the total value of exports was only 62,827,990 yuan, only about 45 percent of imports. Compared with the major trade deficit countries in the world in the same year, China's ratio of import trade to export trade is the lowest in the world. If exports can be increased in the future, the international trade situation will gradually tend towards balance. The Ministry's statistics for the import and export trade and their ratios for major trade deficit countries in the world in 1933 are recorded below: China's import amount: 275,976 (unit: thousand US dollars, same below); export amount: 125,119; the export amount accounts for 45 percent of the import amount. Switzerland's import amount: 299,300; export amount: 158,300; the export amount accounts for 53 percent of the import amount. The United Kingdom's import amount: 2,073,300; export amount: 1,213,000; the export amount accounts for 6 percent of the import amount. France's import amount: 1,117,300; export amount: 724,300; the export amount accounts for 65 percent of the import amount. Austria's import amount: 128,300; export amount: 86,300; the export amount accounts for 67 percent of the import amount. Italy's import amount: 390,300; export amount: 315,300; the export amount accounts for 81 percent of the import amount. Belgium's import amount: 411,300; export amount: 391,300; the export amount accounts for 95 percent of the import amount. Japan's import amount: 380,300; export amount: 366,300; the export amount accounts for 96 percent of the import amount.

Soaring Rice Prices in Anqing, Public Security Bureau Requests Restriction on Purchasing and Transporting 60

Anqing Dispatch: In Anhui Province, after the disaster of famine, it is now the spring famine season. In recent months, rice merchants in the provincial capital have resumed purchasing large quantities of rice for transportation out of the province, causing rice prices to rise sharply, threatening the people's food supply. The Provincial Capital Public Security Bureau has specially requested the Provincial Government to follow the established precedent and restrict purchasing and transporting. The original request is as follows: "We have investigated that various counties in our province are frequently experiencing floods and droughts. The rural areas near the provincial capital are suffering severely. In previous years, due to food shortages, rice riots occurred. Afterwards, rice was purchased from other areas and provided at affordable prices to relieve the situation, and the riots subsided. Last year's autumn harvest in various counties was still poor, and rice prices were high, no less than in previous years. Even the existing rice in this city is already insufficient to meet demand. Furthermore, rice merchants, disregarding the people's food supply, are purchasing large quantities of rice every day for transportation out of the province. According to recent investigations, from the first day of this month to the twentieth, major steamships have transported a total of 4,578 shi (a unit of dry volume) of rice. Small steamships and sailing vessels are not included. This has caused rice prices to soar, reaching ten yuan per shi. In the aftermath of the disaster and during the spring famine, the sudden increase in rice prices is unbearable for the people. If restrictions are not implemented, rice riots may be repeated in the future. This would directly harm the people's food supply and indirectly affect public order. The Director of the Public Security Bureau, filled with anxieties, cannot remain silent. We propose that your government follow the past precedents of prohibiting rice and issue a strict ban, and restrict the amount of rice that each steamship and sailing vessel passing through can purchase and transport. Large steamships should not exceed six shi, small steamships should not exceed two shi, large sailing vessels should not exceed one shi, and small sailing vessels should not exceed five dou (a smaller unit of dry volume). If these limits are violated, the rice being transported will be confiscated in its entirety, and the transporting merchants and civilians will be punished to maintain the people's food supply and preserve public order. This is our responsibility. Therefore, we respectfully submit this document to your government for review and implementation." (March 24)

Wujiang: Huang Heng, the former secretary and chief of the fourth section of the County's Anti-Opium Committee, was secretly investigated by the Jiangsu Provincial Commissioner of Inspection, and it was discovered that Huang had accepted a bribe of 1,800 yuan from local opium trafficker Cai Zhen. County Magistrate Xu sent personnel to Suzhou to place Huang under the custody of the Security Team headquarters, awaiting the commissioner's disposition. Yesterday, the County Government received a telegram from the commissioner ordering that the matter be handled according to the law. County Magistrate Xu, being concurrently in charge of judicial affairs, reasonably recused himself. He immediately dispatched police officers to escort Huang Heng and the case files to the Suzhou Higher Court, designating the relevant agency to handle the matter.

Educational Broadcast Special Issue

The Importance and Promotion of the Cooperative Movement (Part 1) - Dean of the Cooperative College of the Central Political School 70

— Shou Miancheng

(I) The Meaning and Types of Cooperatives

The cooperative movement is a movement to promote the cooperative system. But what is a cooperative? Simply put, a cooperative is an organization that, in the spirit of equality and mutual assistance, voluntarily unites the efforts of a number of people to improve the lives of these people and to improve the economic situation of the entire society.

Comparing a cooperative with general business methods, it can be said that cooperatives have five characteristics:

Equal Equity: Ordinary joint-stock companies are based on the shareholders' capital, and the larger the share capital, the greater the power, so the shareholders can control everything. Cooperatives are not like this, their power is distributed on a per-person basis; any member, regardless of the amount of capital they have paid, is limited to one vote.

Open Organization: Companies with the purpose of doing business generally have a fixed amount of capital, and only within this amount can their shares be bought and become a shareholder. Therefore, the price of shares often changes with the prosperity and decline of the business. If the business is booming, it is necessary to pay a high price to buy its shares. Cooperatives are not like this, their members can join at any time, and the capital is unlimited, so their shares will not [] in price.

Limited Dividends: Because dividends are the income of property, and there are many elements of unearned income in it, cooperatives often have dividend restrictions. Ordinary companies also have dividend regulations, but they are often relatively high. Moreover, the profits of general companies are enjoyed by the shareholders, so even if the dividend restriction is low, it is not very meaningful.

Return of Profits: I have already said above that the profits of a company are enjoyed by the shareholders, but cooperatives are different. The profits that it settles annually or semi-annually are returned to where they came from. Only in this way can price fairness be achieved and mutual exploitation be avoided.

Social Purpose: Cooperatives are organized to seek the interests of their members, just like companies are organized to seek the interests of their shareholders, seemingly without difference. However, the shares of cooperatives are very small, the equity is equal, the organization is open, and the profit distribution method is different, so in practice, it is very different from companies. The purpose of a company is to make money, while the purpose of a cooperative is to seek social benefits.

The above is the meaning of cooperatives. As for their types, the more important ones are production cooperatives, utility cooperatives, purchasing cooperatives, marketing cooperatives, consumer cooperatives, credit cooperatives, and insurance cooperatives. The nature of each type of cooperative will be explained separately below.

Production Cooperative: Production is the act of creating or increasing utility to meet social needs. Therefore, a production cooperative is a group of people who unite their strength to engage in the increase or creation of utility based on the meaning of cooperation. Examples include cooperation in breeding, planting, and processing in the agricultural sector, and cooperation in construction and manufacturing in the industrial sector.

Utility Cooperative: It is where many people unite to jointly purchase and use production equipment, such as water pumps, rice harvesters, seeders, and trucks, to compensate for the lack of individual financial resources and to seek economy of use.

Purchasing Cooperative: It is where production supplies, such as seeds, raw materials, and fertilizers, are purchased jointly, using wholesale methods to reduce prices and reduce miscellaneous expenses.

Marketing Cooperative: After production is completed, a group of people unite their products to jointly transport and sell them, in order to raise prices and reduce costs. It is also called a sales cooperative.

Consumer Cooperative: The term consumer cooperative usually refers only to the joint purchase of consumer goods. The consumer cooperatives or cooperative stores that we often see are only purchasing cooperatives for consumer goods. In fact, cooperation in consumer behavior, such as cooperative cafeterias and cooperative housing, should also be called consumer cooperation, so the former can be said to be broad consumer cooperation, and the latter can be said to be narrow consumer cooperation.

Credit Cooperative: Personal credit is not enough, so a group of people unite their credit to achieve their goals, that is credit cooperation. For example, if twenty people join together to form a loan group and borrow money from a bank, each person bears joint and several liability, that is, if one person is unable to repay the debt, the others must be responsible for repayment. This is also a kind of credit cooperation. With this guarantee of joint liability, it is not only possible to obtain loans, but also to not have to provide collateral, which is not good? However, a true credit cooperative should also be able to absorb the deposits of its members, so that the money deposited by some members can be lent to members who need loans. Therefore, a credit cooperative is like a miniature bank. Of course, the profit distribution methods of banks and credit cooperatives are different. Because the profits of a bank are only distributed to the shareholders, while the profits of a credit cooperative, in addition to dividends and reserve funds, are distributed to the depositors and borrowers, because the profits of a credit cooperative come from them.

Insurance Cooperative: The insurance industry has not yet developed in China, but in foreign countries, half of the people have life insurance, and many houses have fire insurance. The reason for wanting insurance is to distribute the risks of a few people to many people in order to reduce the burden of risk. Because, based on the meaning of interest rates or chance rates, if many people buy insurance, it is unlikely that everyone will encounter danger. However, insurance companies aim to make profits, and the insurance premiums they charge are very high. If many people can unite and use cooperative methods to insure themselves, then the benefits obtained are the same, and the insurance premiums can be saved a lot. Moreover, insurance companies do not distribute profits, while the profits of a cooperative can be distributed, which is also an advantage of insurance cooperatives.

(II) The Importance of Cooperative Enterprises

Speaking of the importance of cooperative enterprises, it can be explained in three points:

First, from the perspective of economic policy, the goal of economic policy is, first, to increase production efficiency, and second, to achieve fair distribution of wealth. There are several conditions for increasing efficiency: land improvement, capital accumulation, labor effort, and strict organization, which are the most important. From these conditions, we can see the importance of cooperative enterprises. Because the utility cooperative mentioned above is a method to improve land and increase labor efficiency. In addition, credit cooperatives can help with capital accumulation, and the problem of farmers lacking organization is also solved with cooperatives.

Secondly, the development of cooperative enterprises will certainly hinder the interests of the current capitalist class. Therefore, from the perspective of society as a whole, cooperative enterprises, in addition to increasing production efficiency, also have the benefit of making the distribution of wealth fairer, which undoubtedly makes cooperative enterprises a most perfect economic policy. There are two keys to the fact that cooperative enterprises can increase the fairness of social wealth distribution: the first is the union of buying and selling, and the second is the distribution of profits. These two methods can reduce the income of those who originally had a lot, and increase the income of those who originally had too little, so the relationship to wealth distribution is very significant. (To be continued)

Liu Speaks of Smoother Diplomatic Negotiations Due to National Unity

Aviation Donation Amounts for Hotels and Restaurants Must Not Be Included in Bills 76

French Concession Authorities Do Not Interfere with Aviation Donations

According to the Central News Agency, regarding the incident of the French Concession authorities interfering with the solicitation of aviation donations, the General Captain's Office of the China Aviation Association, after inquiring about the situation, received a reply from the Police Department of the French Concession stating that hotels and restaurants were fined for including the donation amount in the bills. If they adhere to the principle of voluntariness, they will not interfere. It is reported that the office has replied, explaining that if there are any inappropriate practices in the future, please notify them in advance so that they can directly notify the relevant parties to avoid incidents and maintain friendship. Please instruct the relevant departments to notify separately to facilitate the process. The office also sent a notice to the Hotel Association, the Restaurant Solicitation Committee, and the hotels and restaurants in the district, enclosing the letter from the French Concession Police and the responsible announcement published by the police in various newspapers, requesting them to follow the prescribed principles, not to include the aforementioned donation amount in the bills, but only to attach a receipt for the National Aviation Salvation Fund, and to work hard to achieve the goal of saving the country and saving oneself, so that the future of the nation and the people will be bright.

According to a news from the Political Department of the French Concession, reports in the local newspapers that the French Concession authorities were obstructing aviation donations are not in line with the facts. The French authorities had no interference in the aviation donation issue from the start. However, there was an agreement with the Aviation Association in advance that the donations must adhere to the concession regulations, which clearly state that the donations must be voluntary and not compulsory. Recently, a small number of stores have been forcing customers to pay donations, so the concession authorities had to correct it. As for other businesses that collect donations in accordance with the principle of voluntary donation, there is no need to be alarmed.

According to the Central News Agency, the General Captain's Office of the China Aviation Association previously received reports from the hotel and restaurant industries that the French Concession Police were interfering with the solicitation of funds for national aviation salvation. After inquiring about the situation, Li Dachao, the Consul General, received a reply from the Police Department of the French Concession stating that hotels and restaurants were punished because they included the donation amount in the bills without following the rule of voluntary donation. If they adhere to the rule of voluntary donation, they will not interfere. It is reported that a reply has been sent, explaining the situation, and requesting the relevant departments to notify separately to facilitate the process.

New Eurasian Beijing-Yunnan Route to Open on April 1 77

However, the Originally Scheduled Airfare Must Be Changed Due to Circumstances

Xi'an to Kunming Estimated at Seven and a Half Hours

The new Beijing-Yunnan route of the Eurasian Aviation Company has been prepared and approved by the Ministry of Communications. It is scheduled to open on April 1. However, due to various reasons, the originally scheduled airfare will not go through Nanchang and Guiyang, but will instead go through Xi'an and Chengdu to reach Kunming. Details of the route, passenger and freight rates, and other information are as follows:

Preparation Completed: The Eurasian Company has been preparing for this route for several months. After the chief of the company's flight group, He En, test-flew a Junkers-style giant aircraft earlier this month, he reported the details to the Ministry of Communications for review. Last week, the company's secretary, Zha Zhenwu, went to Beijing to consult with the Ministry of Communications regarding the opening of the route. The Ministry of Communications approved the official opening on April 1.

Change of Route: The original route was scheduled to go from Nanjing through Hankou, Changsha, Nanchang, and Guiyang to Kunming. However, after the test flight, it was decided to change the route due to the poor climate in Guiyang, the long rainy season, the difficult terrain of high mountains and deep valleys, and other reasons. The new route will go from Xi'an through Chengdu to Kunming. The Xi'an station will be connected to the company's Shanghai-Xinjiang route, so although the route has been changed, transportation between Beijing and Yunnan can still be connected.

Flight Schedule: The northbound flight is scheduled to depart from Kunming at 1:00 PM every Wednesday and Saturday, arrive in Chengdu at 4:30 PM, stop in Chengdu overnight, and depart from Chengdu at 8:00 AM on Thursday, arriving in Xi'an at 11:00 AM. The southbound flight is scheduled to depart from Xi'an at 2:00 PM every Tuesday and Friday, arrive in Chengdu at 5:00 PM, depart from Chengdu at 8:00 AM every Wednesday and Saturday, and arrive in Kunming at 11:30 AM. The flight schedule of this route is connected to the schedules of the company's other routes. It is estimated that it will take only seven and a half hours to reach Kunming from Xi'an.

Passenger Fare: Passenger fare table: One-way fare: Shanghai to Kunming 580 yuan, Nanjing to Kunming 550 yuan, Zhengzhou to Kunming 490 yuan, Xi'an to Kunming 425 yuan, Lanzhou to Kunming 605 yuan, Ningxia to Kunming 745 yuan, Baotou to Kunming 875 yuan, Beiping to Kunming 555 yuan, Chengdu to Kunming 200 yuan. Round-trip fare: Shanghai to Kunming 1044 yuan, Nanjing to Kunming 999 yuan, Zhengzhou to Kunming 882 yuan, Xi'an to Kunming 765 yuan, Lanzhou to Kunming 1089 yuan, Ningxia to Kunming 1341 yuan, Baotou to Kunming 1575 yuan, Beiping to Kunming 999 yuan, Chengdu to Kunming 360 yuan.

Route Freight: Route mileage: Shanghai to Kunming 2580 kilometers, Nanjing to Kunming 2320 kilometers, Zhengzhou to Kunming 1750 kilometers, Xi'an to Kunming 1300 kilometers, Lanzhou to Kunming 1800 kilometers, Ningxia to Kunming 2180 kilometers, Baotou to Kunming 2600 kilometers, Beiping to Kunming 2380 kilometers, Chengdu to Kunming 680 kilometers. Freight rate: Shanghai to Kunming 5.80 yuan, Nanjing to Kunming 5.50 yuan, Zhengzhou to Kunming 4.90 yuan, Xi'an to Kunming 4.25 yuan, Lanzhou to Kunming 6.05 yuan, Ningxia to Kunming 7.45 yuan, Baotou to Kunming 8.75 yuan, Beiping to Kunming 5.55 yuan, Chengdu to Kunming 2.00 yuan. The above are the prices per kilogram.

According to the Central News Agency, regarding the incident of Communists hiding in Fudan University in Jiangwan, the Shanghai Garrison Command capturing seven people, and the Communists opening fire and injuring policemen, Mayor Wu instructed before departing for Beijing the night before last to continue searching for the reactionary elements who opened fire yesterday. At around 6:00 AM yesterday morning, the security team and the police, together with Qian Xinzhi, the chairman of the board of directors of the school, Li Denghui, the president of the school, and Jin Tongyin, the secretary-general, searched the interior of the school. The security team and the police withdrew from the school yesterday afternoon. Also, one of the policemen who was injured the day before yesterday, Hou Shengzhen, who belonged to the Jiangwan Police Station, died of his injuries at the Red Cross Hospital at 3:00 PM yesterday afternoon. It is reported that his injury was caused by a gunshot wound. During the search of Fudan University yesterday, many bullet casings were found, including handgun bullets.

Municipal Public Bonds: Principal Repayment Lottery Held Yesterday Morning 83

Seven Lottery Tickets Were Drawn, Repaying a Total of 246,000 Yuan in Principal and Interest

Payment to Be Made by Central, China, Communications, and Municipal Banks Starting at the End of This Month

The Shanghai Municipal Government's municipal public bonds held their eleventh principal repayment lottery at the Bankers Association at 11:00 AM yesterday morning. This time, seven lottery tickets were drawn, repaying a total of 246,000 yuan in principal and interest. The details of the lottery are as follows:

Participating Representatives: Those who attended included Xu Fu, Director of the Municipal Finance Bureau (represented by Xia Maoxin, Chief of the Third Section of the bureau), Li Zhi of the Shanghai Municipal Bank, Wu Bicai of the Municipal Government, Liu Pu of the Central Bank, Gu Yikang of the Municipal Treasury, Lin Jinyu of the Audit Office, Shen Juemou of the Zhejiang Industrial Bank, Wang Huaifen of the Ministry of Finance, Jin Runyang of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, Zhang Zi of the Shanghai Local Court, Fan Jietang of the Foundation Management Committee, Mu Tang of the Bank of Communications, Cao Zhenzhao of the Bank of China, and more than seventy others.

Chairman's Report: After the formalities were completed, the chairman first gave a report, stating in brief: "Today is the eleventh principal repayment lottery for the Shanghai Municipal Public Bonds. We are very fortunate to have you all here to supervise. These public bonds were issued in October of the 18th year of the Republic of China, with a total amount of 3 million yuan. After repaying the principal of 2.1 million yuan, there is a remaining principal of 900,000 yuan. This time, seven tickets will be drawn, repaying a principal of 246,000 yuan. All the winning bonds and the interest due this period will be paid by the Central, China, Communications, and Shanghai Municipal Banks starting on March 31st of this year. Please, supervisors, check the lottery tickets and the lottery ticket register for execution of the lottery."

Seven Tickets Drawn: After the chairman's report, lottery personnel designated from the guests conducted the lottery. Each time a ticket was drawn, it was sent to the chairman for inspection and then to the supervisors for verification. The winning numbers were then announced on a hanging sign, and the registrar recorded them. The supervisors rechecked the winning ticket numbers and added a seal to the ticket register for verification. The winning ticket numbers are as follows: "101", "18", "21", "51", "69", "78", "81".
