Chinese Merchants Emphasize Chinese in Insurance Policies; The Machinery Union Requests Explicit Regulations 88

The Shanghai General Association of Domestic Machinery Factories yesterday petitioned the Executive Yuan to stipulate in the Insurance Law that Chinese insurance policies issued by Chinese merchants should be the standard. The original text reads: "Regarding the clauses listed in the insurance policies of Chinese insurance companies, they all contain the phrase 'English shall prevail.' We earnestly request that this be forwarded to the Legislative Yuan for discussion and amendment of the Insurance Law. At the second meeting of the ninth session of our Association held on February 7th of this year, Cai Shengbai, representative of the Meiya Silk Factory, proposed that the insurance policies of Chinese-operated insurance companies are both in Chinese and English, and it is stated that in the event of any discrepancies between the Chinese and English versions, the English version shall prevail. This is indeed humiliating to our national dignity, and since Chinese people do not fully understand English, insurance companies often use the English version to interpret matters in their favor and evade their liability for compensation when misfortune occurs, leaving policyholders at a loss for words. Taking out insurance in this way is no different from throwing money away, without obtaining the actual benefit of insurance. Taking the factories of our Association members as an example, there are too many cases of evasion of compensation liability to count. If we do not petition the central government to include in the Insurance Law the provision that insurance policies used by Chinese insurance companies should be in Chinese, and if other languages are used, it should be clearly stated that the Chinese version shall prevail, then the losses we suffer in insurance matters will know no end." When this was discussed, the atmosphere at the meeting was very tense, and a unanimous resolution was passed. It was noted that our Association had already submitted a petition to the Ministry of Industry for correction on August 21st of last year, and the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce was also requested to persuade the industry to make corrections, as recorded in the files. Subsequently, a reply was received from the Ministry of Industry, ref. Shang Zi No. 37041, stating, "Received your submission. Regarding the case of changing the articles of incorporation of Chinese insurance companies' insurance policies to use Chinese, the Shanghai Civic Federation had already sent a telegram requesting this in August of the 21st year, and an order was issued to the Shanghai Social Affairs Bureau to instruct the Chinese Insurance Industry Association to comply. Now, based on the previous situation, the Bureau has been ordered again to instruct the Insurance Industry Association to comply with the previous case. You are to be informed accordingly." However, the Chamber of Commerce replied with a letter from the Insurance Industry Association, claiming that the insurance policies and receipts had been universally using Chinese for two years, and pointed out that the proposals of Meiya Silk Factory were a misunderstanding. Meiya Silk Factory, based on actual facts, repeatedly refuted this and sent a letter to our Association on September 25th of last year to forward to the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce and the Insurance Industry Association. Unexpectedly, it was not until January 9th of this year that a reply was received from the Association stating, "Received your important instructions regarding the case of Chinese insurance companies changing to using Chinese forms, and am very grateful for your concern. The Legislative Yuan is currently deliberating on the Insurance Law, and the basic terms of this insurance policy will naturally be stipulated therein, which should alleviate your worries." The company's words seem to suggest that the reason why insurance policies are not based on Chinese is because the government has not stipulated it in the Insurance Law. Their tactic of strong arguments and quibbles is the same as their usual way of dealing with policyholders when unfortunate events occur, misinterpreting English and evading compensation liability. It is not known that the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce had already submitted a petition in November of the 19th year to order Chinese insurance policies to be changed to Chinese, and the Civic Federation also submitted a petition in August of the 21st year to order them to be changed to Chinese. Our Association has also repeatedly submitted letters requesting correction, and the Ministry of Industry has repeatedly ordered compliance. Six years have passed, but the insurance policies used by the insurance industry still contain the phrase "English shall prevail." To our countrymen, to our government, this not only violates the public opinion of various organizations and policyholders, but also treats the Ministry's orders as trivial. Their obstinate situation, if not intending to deceive the people by means of foreign languages, who would believe it? Now, with the unanimous resolution of all two hundred and dozens of members, a document is prepared again to petition your esteemed Yuan for review and approval to "forward it to the Legislative Yuan" for discussion and amendment of the Insurance Law, that the insurance policies used by Chinese insurance companies should use Chinese characters, and if other domestic or foreign languages are used, it should be clearly stated that the Chinese shall prevail, so as to prevent the insurance industry from taking advantage of loopholes and to enable policyholders to obtain their due rights and interests. This is for the public benefit. Respectfully submitted.

Telephone Association to Hold Meeting Today to Discuss This Month's Payment Issues; Cui Qingxi Informs of Low Telephone Rates in Britain and America 89

The Ta Kung Pao reports that the Special District Telephone Issue Committee, due to the sudden impact of the new Special District telephone rate system, has aroused widespread opposition. Now, brothels and courtesan houses, unable to bear the burden, have all been dismantled. The brokers' association of the five exchanges has also resolved to deal with the situation, urging the company to realize the problem. The Chinese Ratepayers' Association of the concession, under the pressure of various public organizations, has scheduled a representative assembly next month to discuss solutions. The Association has received numerous letters from users in various districts who, due to the increase in telephone prices, have requested instructions on how to handle the payment issues for January. After receiving the letters, the Association believes that this issue is of great importance and has scheduled the fifth board meeting for 3:00 PM today (the 26th) at the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce, Tianhou Palace Bridge, third floor, and invited advisory committee members to attend and discuss countermeasures together. The Association yesterday received a letter from Cui Qingxi, a Master of Economics from Syracuse University in New York, forwarded by the Foreign Exchange Department of the Central Bank, detailing a comparison of telephone rates in Britain and the United States, which can serve as a basis for negotiation. The original letter stated: "According to the Shanghai Da Mei Evening News of March 10, a spokesman for the Shanghai Telephone Company said, 'A telephone call in the United States costs three US cents, equivalent to 11.1 Chinese cents. A telephone call in Britain costs 6.5 Chinese cents.' In his opinion, foreign gold dollars should be used as a basis for comparing Chinese telephone rates. This is actually a misrepresentation of the facts. Although Britain and the United States use gold dollars, it is only nominally a gold standard, and there are no real gold dollars of equal value as a standard. For example, a single US dollar coin is mostly made of silver, and its weight is even less than that of a Chinese silver dollar, but its price is equivalent to 3.33 Chinese dollars (current market price). The so-called US telephone fee of three cents per call, equivalent to 11.1 Chinese cents, is a great fallacy. If you use the Chinese exchange rate to accurately compare, using it in the United States is equivalent to using three copper coins in Shanghai. Because in the United States, the cent is the smallest unit, and there is no smaller auxiliary currency below the cent, and the US single-cent auxiliary currency is also made of copper, and its weight is less than a quarter of that of a Chinese copper coin. However, a telephone call in Shanghai costs three cents each time, which is actually equivalent to nine US cents. The telephone fee for residents in Syracuse, New York, is only three dollars per month, and they can make unlimited calls. The telephone fees in Britain and France are even lower than those in the United States. Therefore, the telephone fee in Shanghai is actually several times higher than that in Britain and the United States. As for the legal aspect, although the regulations on concession contracts for public utilities in various countries around the world are slightly different, they are roughly divided into three types: Perpetual concession contracts. This type of contract is announced and implemented by the court and does not indicate restrictions on events. Very few are currently used, and they have almost disappeared invisibly. Short-term concession contracts are from the Ministry of Public Security. This type of contract has no fixed term, and it usually expires after about 20 years. If the company is managed properly, it can be extended; otherwise, it can be cancelled. Indefinite contracts. This type of contract has no fixed term, and the main point is that if the company's management does not meet public opinion, the government or citizens can stop its business and take it back at any time at a price. The type of contract of the Shanghai Telephone Company is not clear, but in principle it must be similar. Therefore, the government and legal groups have the right to correct it."

Zhejiang Trade Union Sends Telegram to Zhejiang Provincial Government Offering Suggestions for Consolidating Zhejiang Debt and Requesting a Loan from the Central Bank to Settle Debts 91

The Shanghai Zhejiang Trade Union yesterday telegraphed the Zhejiang Provincial Government, stating, "To the esteemed Zhejiang Provincial Government: According to the telegrams from the Hangzhou Banking Industry Association and the Hangzhou Money Industry Association, which stated, in brief, that the bonds issued by this province include the Public Bonds to Repay Old Debts, Highway Public Bonds, Construction Public Bonds, Disaster Relief Public Bonds, Public Bonds for Clearing Old Debts, Provincial Treasury Bonds, and Local Public Bonds, totaling seven types. The Finance Department of the Provincial Government has borrowed more than 11 million yuan from the banking and money industries. Recently, the Finance Department has proposed to reduce the interest rates on various bonds, extend the principal, and change the terms of various loans, considering the contracts invalid and hindering the social credit system. Please make a unanimous appeal to maintain credit. We have learned that the various bonds of this province have reached more than 45 million yuan, requiring a huge amount of annual interest. Therefore, they must be urgently consolidated to achieve a suitable balance between the province's budget revenues and expenditures, so as to avoid further increasing the burden on the people. The issuance of bonds in this province has always been levied on the people of various counties, unlike the issuance of various central government bonds, which are exclusively underwritten by the banking industry. Moreover, the public welfare, education, and charitable funds of various counties have always been used for storage and interest, and now they are all used to purchase public bonds. If the reduction of interest and extension of principal are implemented, the local affairs of various counties will be affected. Besides, in this time of financial hardship, reducing debt to save expenses is a key plan for the present, but the government and the people should consider both. Considering that the Central Bank is a national bank with the power to issue currency and actually controls the general hub of national finance, and that the debts of this province are so huge, all due to the construction of railways, highways, and military facilities, these undertakings are related to national defense and should not be the sole responsibility of one province, we should request that the Ministry of Finance order the Central Bank to lend 50 million yuan in national currency, using the existing bond funds of this province as security, setting the lowest interest rate, and repaying the principal and interest in installments. On the one hand, all seven types of bonds issued in this province should be redeemed in advance so that bondholders do not suffer any losses, and the government can save millions of principal and interest annually, and the special construction tax can be stopped as scheduled. Various surcharges that are nearly chaotic can also be cut down year by year. Upon checking, the funds for various bonds in this province are salt surtax, special construction tax, construction surcharge, and ordinary business tax, totaling 6,801,402 yuan in the Zhejiang Provincial Budget for the 24th year. The funds for local public bonds are designated as daily land tax, deed tax, brokerage business tax, and tobacco and alcohol license tax, with an annual allocation of 1.2 million yuan. In total, the funds for various bonds amount to 8,001,402 yuan. Since the Central Government has already issued a clear order to reduce interest rates, the Central Bank should first implement low-interest loans. If calculated at a weekly interest rate of 4%, the annual cost would be 2 million yuan. If another 1 million yuan of annual bond principal is allocated, 5 million yuan can be gained from the funds. Therefore, this loan is exceptionally solid and the funds are exceptionally substantial, so it should not be rejected. In this way, turning scattered debt into a whole only requires moving and transferring debt, which can preserve credit and hopefully reduce the burden on the people. We offer our humble opinions. We respectfully request your esteemed government to review and adopt them for implementation, which would be for the public convenience. Respectfully, the Shanghai Zhejiang Trade Union."

Chen Jintao Lectures on "Sun Yat-sen's Paper Money Revolution" at the Business School Yesterday 93

The Central News Agency reports that Chen Jintao, Chairman of the Currency System Committee of the Ministry of Finance, gave a lecture at the National Shanghai Business School yesterday on "Sun Yat-sen's Paper Money Revolution." Chen traced the motives and plans of Mr. Sun Yat-sen in advocating paper money, and praised and criticized it from a historical perspective, listing the precedents of the paper money revolution in European and American countries, most notably the gradual implementation of Gesell's Stamp Scrip plan. He also said that this time, our country's implementation of the new monetary policy, concentrating silver and promoting legal tender, is only carrying out Mr. Sun Yat-sen's legacy. Cheng Shaode, the Dean of Studies of the Business School, revealed to us the historical anecdotes of the theory of paper money revolution, which has special value in the history of monetary development in China. The case of Kunqu performer Ding Wan'e and her husband Yang Binghua being sued by their apprentice, female performer Tan Lianfen, in the First Special District Court for illegal detention has been reported in this newspaper. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Jiang Shuzi continued the trial in the Second Criminal Court. Witnesses Zhao Chunfang, Ding Shaolan, and Kuai Qixiang all appeared in court. According to Zhao, who claimed to be mainly a Shenqu singer, on February 14, the defendant ordered him to perform at a private gathering. Unexpectedly, after arriving at the defendant's house, he was accused of having an affair with Tan Lianfen and was forced to write a letter of guarantee. He saw the defendant beat the plaintiff, but he had no real relationship with Tan. Ding Shaolan testified that she had separated from Ding Wan'e for seven or eight years. Zhao Chunfang was already there and wrote a letter of repentance, asking her to act as an intermediary and sign her name on the letter of guarantee. She did not see the defendant beat the plaintiff. Kuai Qixiang testified that he also acted as an intermediary. Tan Lianfen testified that the witnesses' statements were partially correct and partially incorrect. She was sent to the defendant's house by Ding Shaolan that day and was immediately beaten and locked in a room. She had no real relationship with Zhao, only acquaintanceship. Ding Wan'e and Yang Binghua testified that because their reputation was involved, they used the pretext of singing at a private gathering to lure Zhao to their house. Zhao voluntarily wrote the letter of guarantee because he could not afford to marry Tan. Tax Administration Sends Letter to Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce Requesting Correction of Flower Tax Stickers for Hall Passes and Bureau Tickets 95

The National Tax Administration of the Ministry of Finance yesterday sent a letter to the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce stating: "It has been found that Article 16 of the current Stamp Tax Law, Tax Rate Table, Item 23, under the category of entertainment tickets, specifies that all tickets sold by entertainment venues for admission or seating are included. Hall passes and bureau tickets are not tickets sold by entertainment venues for admission or seating and are not within the scope of this item. They should be affixed with ordinary stamps. However, it has recently been found that some hotels in the concession still charge customers for stamps on bureau tickets, as stipulated in the temporarily abolished Stamp Regulations, but in reality, they do not affix the stamps. This behavior clearly involves fraud. In addition to ordering the Shanghai Concession Cigarette Investigation Office to conduct a thorough investigation and instructing the Shanghai urban area stamp tax inspectors to pay attention to whether the same situation occurs in various hotels in the urban area and to investigate them together, we hereby send a letter to your esteemed association for your information and request that you instruct the Shanghai Hotel Industry Association to inquire about individual hotels and correct them to maintain the credit of national taxes."

Tragedy Occurs Before Birthday Banquet; Police Officer at Linping Road Police Station Commits Suicide by Shooting Due to Nervous Breakdown 97

At around 12:00 PM yesterday, a police officer committed suicide by shooting at the Civilian Village Police Substation of the Linping Road Police Station of the Zhabei North Station Branch. After being discovered, he was rushed to Tongren Hospital for treatment. Due to the severity of his injuries, he died at around 1:00 PM in the afternoon. The reasons for the police officer's despair were economic pressure and family issues. The details are as follows:

Police Officer's Family

Yin Fukang, from Yancheng, was 34 years old. His home was at 5 Zao Pi Alley, Jun'an Lane, Tianbao Road, Zhabei. Yin lost his father at a young age, and his elderly mother, nearly 80 years old, lives in his hometown, Qijia Village, about two li from Ligangmen Town. Yin's first wife died early, and he remarried Wu Xiaomao, a woman from his hometown, as his second wife at the beginning of last year. Wu is 24 years old. After the marriage, she gave birth to a son, whose milk name is Huaisheng, who is two years old. Yin previously served as a police officer in the Fourth Precinct of the Fifth District of the Municipal Public Security Bureau (now the Yuanguan Xianggang Police Station). In the 17th year of the Republic of China, he was transferred to the Linping Road Police Station (formerly the Third Precinct of the Fifth District), where he served as a second-class police officer with badge number 2704. He has served in various substations under the jurisdiction. Yin was thrifty and diligent in his service and was deeply valued by his superiors. He also got along well with his colleagues.

Economic Pressure

Yin received a monthly salary of 16 yuan while serving in the police station. Family expenses exceeded income, and he felt deeply burdened by economic pressure, which often led to quarrels with his second wife, Wu. In order to save expenses, Yin sent Wu and his son Huaisheng back to their hometown to stay temporarily last winter. Unexpectedly, the family's flesh and blood were separated from then on, resulting in a tragic turn of events.

Shooting Suicide

At the beginning of this month, Yin was transferred by the station chief, Niu Jingquan, to the Civilian Village Police Substation. Yin was very filial to his mother, and her 80th birthday was on the 29th of this month. He distributed invitations to friends, planning to hold a banquet at the Dafugui Restaurant to celebrate. Unexpectedly, at around 12:00 PM yesterday, while Yin was wiping his pistol in the dining room of the Civilian Village Police Substation, he suddenly felt a nervous breakdown and pointed the gun at his chest and pulled the trigger. With a loud bang, smoke filled the room. The bullet entered from the right chest and exited from the back, and he fell to the ground. Blood flowed out. The police officers on duty rushed to the scene upon hearing the sound. Yin was barely breathing. They immediately reported to the police chief and called an ambulance to take Yin to Tongren Hospital for treatment. However, the bullet hit a vital spot, and his injuries were too severe. He died at around 1:00 PM in the afternoon. The hospital then notified the station.

Court Inspection

Upon hearing the news, the station immediately ordered bailiffs to move Yin's body to the temporary mortuary of the Tianbao Road Stack Industry Association. The local chief reported to the local court, which sent prosecutor Xiao Jinying, along with clerk Zhang Guowei and judicial police officers, to the scene at around 5:30 PM to verify the death. It was determined that he died from a gunshot wound. The body was properly prepared for burial.

Request for Compensation

All the officers and police of the Linping Road Police Station believe that Yin had served in the station for many years, was diligent in his duties, and suffered a tragic event. They plan to jointly petition the headquarters to request compensation. Yin's elderly mother, wife, and children are all in his hometown, and they have been notified by telegram to come to Shanghai to handle the aftermath.

Customs to Fire Noon Cannon Every Wednesday and Saturday; Shanghai Residents Can Obtain Accurate Time 98

The North-China Daily News reports that, in order to allow Shanghai residents to obtain accurate time, the open space of the Jianghai Customs building opposite the Bund Jianghai Customs building will use a sixty-year-old discarded cannon to fire a twelve-pound live shell every Wednesday and Saturday at noon, making a sound to inform the public. At around 11:50 AM on these two days, the employees of the signal station will install gunpowder. When they see the large ball on top of the signal mast on the Bund descend, they will ignite the fuse, and the sound will be heard immediately. In addition, residents who want to know the accurate time can dial the automatic telephone number 95678 to inquire with the telephone company and receive a reply immediately. Moreover, the "astronomical clock" placed by the Shanghai Electric Power Company in Jiangbin relies on the connected wires to adjust the time from time to time for all public and private electric clocks in the concession. This astronomical clock is made accurate by the priests of the Xujiahui Observatory. Furthermore, a certain radio station broadcasts the time on the hour throughout the day to benefit residents who do not have electric clocks. With these various conveniences, Shanghai residents can avoid the risk of being late.

The Machine Industry Association Presents a Petition to the Ministry of Railways, Requesting the Balancing of Freight Rates 100

Excessive Railway Freight Rates Hinder the Development of National Goods; Request for Deliberation on Commercial Conditions to Balance Freight Rates

The Shanghai Machine-Made National Goods Factories Joint Association, based on letters from member factories such as the Senlin Rattan, Willow, and Grass Ware Factory, stating that excessive railway freight rates hinder the development of national goods sales, specially submitted a petition to the Ministry of Railways yesterday. They requested the ministry to deliberate on international commercial conditions and balance freight rates. A Xin Xin News Agency reporter recorded the original petition as follows: "Presenting a petition regarding the excessive collection of railway freight affecting sales, requesting deliberation on international commercial conditions to balance freight rates to benefit national goods. According to a letter from member factories such as the Senlin Rattan, Willow, and Grass Ware Factory, the various manufactured goods produced by our factories, such as grass mats (commonly known as grass carpets, made of grass), foot pads (i.e., doormats made of coconut fiber), cotton carpets (made of waste cotton), as well as rattan and bamboo ware, are sold in various ports such as Beijing, Tianjin, Pingqing, and are transported by railway. The railway bureau designates grass mats as grass products and charges them at the fourth-class rate. If they are declared as ordinary fine mats, they will be penalized. However, these grass mats are actually coarser than ordinary fine mats. For example, the selling price of each ordinary coarse mat is 70 cents, so five mats are worth $3.50. However, a grass mat is five times thicker than an ordinary coarse mat, and its selling price is only $1.80. In addition to the railway freight rate for ordinary coarse mats being classified as fifth-class, there is also the benefit of a special price that does not measure dimensions. Why must grass mats be charged at the fourth-class rate for grass products? We should request that it be changed to fifth-class, according to the regulations for ordinary coarse mats. This is the first point. The railway bureau classifies the freight rate for foreign foot pads as second-class. Our factory's foot pads are also calculated as second-class. Therefore, for $100 worth of goods shipped to Tianjin, Pingqing, the freight is as expensive as $18, which has led to the flooding of Japanese goods in those places. We should request the railway bureau to reduce it to a considerable extent. This is another point. The value of cotton carpets and wool carpets varies greatly, but the freight rate is the same for both, at third-class. We should request the railway bureau to change the cotton carpets to fourth-class to show the distinction. This is another point. As for rattan and bamboo ware, only the weight was measured in the past, not the dimensions. For example, the freight for one piece of rattan and bamboo ware shipped to distant places such as Tianjin, Pingqing, and even Fengtian and Harbin, was only $1. Now the railway bureau classifies it as fourth-class and also measures the dimensions. If it is shipped to various places such as Tianjin and Pingqing, the value of one piece of rattan and bamboo ware is limited, but the freight is as high as $6. If this rattan and bamboo ware is shipped from Shanghai to Qingdao and Dalian by Japanese ships, the freight charge is only 40 Japanese sen, which is equivalent to 54 cents in national currency. Therefore, our factory's rattan and bamboo ware used to sell 50,000 to 60,000 yuan a year along the railway line, but after the implementation of dimensional charging, it disappeared. We should request the railway bureau to examine international commercial conditions and the actual difficulties of national goods, and specially reduce freight rates to facilitate sales throughout the country and compete with foreign goods. This is another point. Currently, our factory's products, such as Japanese grass mats and foot pads, are shipped from Kobe to any port in our country and are calculated at 46 cubic feet (i.e., one ton) for freight, charging only 3 Japanese yen. National goods, on the other hand, are charged more than 10 yuan, even more than 20 yuan. If we do not receive the railway bureau's understanding, the market trade will be completely seized. We have long admired your association's tireless efforts to seek outlets for the products of member factories. We are now reporting the fact that railway freight is too heavy and asking for your assistance," etc., were sent to the association. The two railway administrations of the Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo lines under your ministry aim to take into account production, sales, and transportation to seek the development of railway transportation. The intention is excellent. However, the products produced by the Senlin Factory are transported by the railway bureau, which is a heavy burden. This greatly hinders the prospects for production, sales, and transportation. In addition to writing to the railway bureau, we are now reporting the situation to you, hoping that your ministry will deliberate on a reduction to increase the railway bureau's income and benefit the production and sales of national goods. This is truly a matter of public convenience." Respectfully submitted to the Railway Department of the National Government of the Republic of China.

Two Criminals Sentenced to Fifteen Years Each for Illegally Selling Heroin; Two Koreans Sent to Japanese Consulate for Interrogation 103

Highly potent drugs such as morphine, heroin, cocaine, and red pills are able to circulate in the market because of their potent nature, which is far superior to opium, and their price is cheaper than opium. Therefore, poor people with a smoking addiction abandon opium and consume drugs. It must be known that the harm of drugs is even worse than floods and beasts. Once addicted, there is no hope of quitting, and it can reduce a person's lifespan. Therefore, the Anti-Smoking Commissioner has promulgated special provisions, stipulating that those who sell, manufacture, and transport drugs will be sentenced to the most severe punishment. The old Zha division of the Public Concession of this city has many small inns, and many of the travelers who live there are peddlers and vagrants addicted to drugs. Drug traffickers also use this area as a concentration area. Because of the strict investigation and prohibition by the division, they often rely on foreign ronin as a talisman. The division, aware of their tricks, ordered Chief Inspector You Agen to strictly arrest them. There have been repeated crackdowns, and they have been handed over to the First Special Court and severely punished. At 9:50 PM the night before, Chen Zifu from Shaoxing was selling heroin in the Yong'anfang on Edward Road. At that time, Wu Wencheng from Hebei stepped forward and bought three packets from Lu. While they were trading, they were discovered by Chinese Controller Ping Xiushan, Bao Detective Sun Dafa, and Chinese Constable No. 2291 of the old Zha division. They immediately arrested the two men and took them back to the division along with the three packets of heroin. Under strict interrogation, Lu confessed that the sales agency was located at No. 606 Edward Road. The detectives rushed to search the premises and arrested two Koreans, Cui Jingfu and Han Changdong, and a man from Suzhou, Yan Fugen (also known as Agen). One hundred and thirty-two packets of heroin were found behind Cui's coat, and a morphine syringe was found on the bed. In addition to sending the two Koreans to the Japanese Consulate, the other three, Wu Wencheng, Lu Zifu, and Yan Fugen, were sent to the First Special District Court's Criminal Division 1 yesterday morning. The division's lawyer, Wang Yaotang, explained the case and prosecuted them according to Articles 263 and 257 of the Criminal Law, requesting that they be severely punished according to the law so that those engaged in this career would be intimidated. After Qian Hongye, the Presiding Judge of the Criminal Court, rigorously questioned the defendants, he announced the judgment in court: Wu Wencheng was sentenced to forty days of detention, and Lu Zifu and Yan Fugen were each sentenced to fifteen years of imprisonment, each deprived of public rights for ten years, and the three packets of heroin were confiscated.

The Lawyers' Association and the Banking Association Exchange Letters to Improve the Reasons for Returning Checks 104

The exchange of letters between the Shanghai Lawyers' Association and the Shanghai Banking Association is recorded below: The Shanghai Lawyers' Association wrote in its letter: "Dear Sirs, The proposal of member He Jia states that ordinary banks, when returning checks due to insufficient funds or no funds, often write the vague phrase 'Please contact the drawer' on the reason for return slip. If the parties are involved in litigation due to the returned check, it will take more court investigation procedures, which will greatly delay the progress of the case. This is to save the face of the drawer, but it affects the interests of the other party to a considerable extent. Therefore, it is proposed that your association decide to consult the banking association to notify all banks that in the future, the reason for the returned check must be clearly written to facilitate enforcement and avoid the lawyer's case handling process. The meeting of the joint executive and supervisory committees of this association deliberated and decided that since there is a column for insufficient funds on the reason for return slip, it should be filled in truthfully to avoid increasing disputes and losses. The financial community should inform the banking and money industries associations to notify all member banks to pay attention to writing it clearly on record. In addition to sending separate letters, we hereby inform you, hoping that your association will inform all member banks to pay attention to writing the reason for the returned check clearly." The Shanghai Banking Association replied in its letter: "Dear Sirs, The proposal of your association's member states that ordinary banks, when returning checks due to insufficient funds or no funds, often write the vague phrase 'Please contact the drawer' on the reason for return slip. If involved in court litigation, it will take more investigation procedures, etc. (omitted). Upon forwarding and consultation, it was submitted to our association's executive committee for discussion. The members believed that there were compelling reasons for banks to use the phrase 'Please contact the drawer' as the reason for returning a check. Banks value business and must be cautious in serving customers. If a depositor deposits money later and the check holder collects money earlier, it is common for them to be different occasionally. If the bank states that the funds are insufficient, it would lose the bank's purpose of facilitating customers. Also, if a depositor thinks that there is a slight balance in the account, the funds may be insufficient to pay. However, for the sake of the customer's reputation and its own business, the bank has to take this into account. From the above two examples, one can see a glimpse of the difficulties. However, to protect the check holder, the bank has never failed to clearly inform depositors who repeatedly issue bad checks that funds are insufficient. It has been found that most of those who are sued for returning checks belong to this category. In fact, it may not take more investigation procedures. Furthermore, after encountering a returned check, if the check holder is unable to reach an agreement with the drawer, they can request the bank to re-present the check and request a change to the insufficient funds reason slip. It seems that all parties can be taken care of. In addition to resolving to circulate the decision to all banks in the association that they should strictly apply the reason for the return of checks for depositors who repeatedly issue bad checks, we are corresponding in reply, hoping that you will investigate and inform them accordingly."

The Directors of the Public Security Bureau and the Consolidated Tax Bureau Jointly Issue a Prohibition on Privately Manufacturing Cigarette Making Equipment 105

Cai Jingjun, Director of the Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau, and Sheng Shengyuan, Director of the Consolidated Tax Bureau of the Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and Anhui District, jointly issued a proclamation yesterday to prohibit the private manufacture, purchase, and transportation of manual cigarette making equipment. The proclamation stated: "It is noted that there are many cigarette factories in the Shanghai urban area, and the private manufacture and sale of manual cigarettes has never been permitted, as it hinders tax revenue. The tools used for cigarettes, such as hand-cranked iron machines and small wooden machines, are even more used by private manufacturers and should be banned altogether to prevent them from spreading. This Consolidated Tax Bureau has now received the Ministry of Finance's 'Regulations on Prohibiting the Private Manufacture, Purchase, and Transportation of Manual Cigarette Making Equipment,' ordering that it be publicly promulgated and implemented immediately. This Public Security Bureau has the responsibility to assist in the investigation and arrest. To make the prohibition clear, the full text of the regulations will be jointly proclaimed for public knowledge. Hereafter, if anyone privately manufactures or uses various cigarette making equipment to supply the manufacture of private cigarettes, they will be strictly dealt with in accordance with Article 4 of the current regulations once they are caught, without leniency. Each must comply and not violate. This is the proclamation."

Barber Pursues Female Customer

Sending threatening letters and helping her escape

Meeting at the Great World to express his love

Claiming to be young and hoping to become a family

——Yuan Zhiguang's lustful audacity results in his on-the-spot arrest——

Yu Jinbao, a local country woman residing in a self-built house at the end of Avenue Joffre in the French Concession, is thirty-two years old this year. In the autumn of the 22nd year of the Republic of China, she married Cai Asan, a local coppersmith who was twenty-four years old, as her husband. Unexpectedly, on the 21st and 24th of this month, she received two postal threatening letters demanding eight hundred yuan, stating that if there was no money, she and her husband would be forced to separate, otherwise they would be bombed. The first meeting was arranged in Room 406 of the Datong Hotel, and the second meeting was arranged in Room 506 of the Dongya Hotel. Yu Jinbao was shocked and reported to the French Police, who ordered detectives to go to the destination to arrest them, but there was no trace of them. The day before yesterday, a neighbor, Tao Ma, came to Yu's house to ask if Yu Jinbao had received any threatening letters, and said that she could be Lu Zhonglian. Yu pretended to entrust her, and then arranged to meet at the Great World Amusement Park. On one hand, Yu reported to the police and ordered Detective Zhou Bingcheng and Detective Zuo Qihong to disguise as tourists and enter the venue to observe the situation. On the other hand, Yu Jinbao went to the Great World as agreed. Sure enough, she saw Ma and another man, Yuan Zhiguang, whom she knew, and Ma's husband, Tao Pucheng, were negotiating. They were all arrested by Detective Zhou and others and taken into the police station. It was found that there was a segment of unrequited pursuit in this case, which led to this interesting scene. Yu Jinbao's father left behind land and property, which belonged to a well-to-do family. Ten years ago, she took Yu Jinnan as her husband, but he died of illness. Thus, Jinbao became a widow at home. However, she often went to the luxurious barbershop set up by her neighbors Tao Pucheng and Tao Ma at No. 1690 Haige Road for haircuts. As a result, she was coveted by the barber Yuan Zhiguang (from Tongzhou, twenty-four years old this year), who repeatedly teased Yu Jinbao. The shop owner Tao Jincheng also instigated him from the sidelines, but unfortunately, it did not suit Yu's wishes. She ignored him and never went to the shop for haircuts again. This happened in the summer of the 23rd year of the Republic of China. In the autumn, Yu married Cai Asan, and the Hua Li barbershop closed down due to economic reasons. Yuan Zhiguang went to work at the Hot Spring Bathhouse on Avenue Edward in the British Concession. However, Yuan Zhiguang's desire to pursue Yu Jinbao was never released. He used these threatening letters to scare Yu, wanting to make Yu separate from Cai Asan and marry him to fulfill his beautiful dream. When Ma arranged for Yu Jinbao to meet at the Great World, Yuan Zhiguang said to Yu Jinbao, "I have been thinking of you for a long time. The name Liu Jianyin on the letters you received is my alias. Cai Asan is twenty-four years old, but I am also twenty-four years old, very young. If you don't mind, you can quickly separate from Cai and marry me," etc. Yu repeatedly said yes. Unexpectedly, the detectives were nearby, and as soon as Yuan finished speaking, Yuan and others were arrested. Yesterday, they were sent to Criminal Division 1 of the Second Special Court. The police lawyer Chen Ming explained the situation and asked for a change of date for investigation. Judge Li Changnian questioned the defendants and then sent them back into custody, setting a date for review on the 30th.

Mr. Yang Guozhu Speaks on Public Preparation for Modern Air Defense 109

Mr. Yang Guozhu, Director of the Research Department of the Chinese Aviation Association, yesterday spoke at the auditorium of the Health Branch of the Shanghai Municipal Council on Hankou Road, at the invitation of the Chinese Staff Club of the Shanghai Municipal Council and other groups. His topic was "Preparations the Public Should Have for Modern Air Defense." About 400 members attended. The lecture lasted about an hour and covered three sections: 1. The role of aviation in past wars; 2. The progress of modern aircraft; and 3. Shanghai's position in a future world war. His speech was pertinent and to the point. In particular, the third section on how citizens should defend against air raids was easy to understand and should be common knowledge for everyone. We have specially extracted and published the main points for reference. "Civilian air defense" refers to the preparations that citizens themselves should make to defend against air raids. Defense methods can be divided into six points: 1. Light control: The first necessary measure when an aircraft attacks a city is to extinguish all lights in the city to eliminate the enemy's targets. The light control measures should not only focus on the city itself, but also on the surrounding suburbs and villages. If the lights in the villages surrounding the city are not extinguished, the enemy aircraft can still identify the location of the city. The method of light control should be proportional to the speed of the aircraft. For example, if the speed of the aircraft is 180 miles per hour, then when the enemy aircraft flies to 90 miles, the lights of the city and surrounding villages must be completely shielded within half an hour. As soon as the watchman's report is received, unnecessary lights on the street must be reduced within five minutes, because the light from electric advertisements in the city can be seen from a hundred miles away. Within ten minutes, all lights outside the door must be turned off. Within fifteen minutes, all indoor lights must be turned off or covered with black cloth, because the enemy aircraft will arrive in another fifteen minutes, and it can already see the city when it is fifteen minutes away, that is, when it flies to four or five miles away. 2. Smoke screen: Most of the current urban buildings are made of cement, so the roofs, walls, and streets are all grayish-white in color. In the dark, due to the reflection effect, they can still be seen even without light. Therefore, to avoid becoming a target for enemy aircraft, a layer of smoke screen must be added. The amount of smoke screen released should be about the same as the amount of air, because if the smoke screen is too light, it will lose its effect after dispersing in the air. However, if it is too thick, it will hinder traffic. Therefore, it is best to release the same amount of smoke screen as air, and the best direction is downwind. 3. Bunkers: In future wars, the enemy's air raids will mostly focus on urban areas, and most urban buildings are about ten stories high. If a thousand-pound bomb is dropped, the high-rise buildings within 500 meters will inevitably collapse. Therefore, it is much better to be underground than on the ground when a city is attacked by aircraft. Building bunkers underground is a place for urban residents to hide. The construction of bunkers is proportional to the population. Private bunkers should be at least seven feet deep, and the top of the bunker should be protected with steel bars for safety. The exit of the bunker should be built at a considerable distance from the house to avoid being blocked by bricks and tiles. Public bunkers in European and American countries are built in parks or other public places. France has now built sixteen tunnels that can connect the center of Paris to the suburbs. 4. Fire fighting: The materials used in urban buildings are mostly flammable. For this reason, enemy aircraft also drop incendiary bombs when bombing cities. With this fire problem, fire fighting must be given extra attention. However, relying solely on the city's fire brigade during air raids is useless. Citizens from all walks of life should prepare fire-fighting equipment and training in fire-fighting techniques in advance, and they can be temporarily organized into districts during wartime. Because there is a possibility of fire everywhere at any time during wartime, it is obviously impossible for the fire brigade to move as usual. Moreover, the depth of urban water pipes is more than five feet. If the water pipes are damaged and the water source is cut off, the citizens will be even more confused. 5. Gas defense: Poison gas already existed during the European War, but it was still in its infancy at that time. However, the progress and intensity of the manufacturing of poison gas now is enough to make people fearful. For example, if one ounce of poison gas is scattered on 50,000 cubic feet of ground, everyone who comes into contact with it will die. In this way, if two tons of poison gas are dropped on Shanghai, which is 26 million cubic feet, then none of the citizens of Shanghai can be spared. Regarding defense methods, you must wear a gas mask outdoors. If you meet someone suddenly, you can temporarily use a wet towel instead, because the acid in poison gas can be neutralized with water. However, this method cannot remedy mustard gas. As for the interior, the most important thing is to isolate the doors and windows from the outside air. To isolate the doors and windows, thick flannel can be used instead of glass. At the necessary entrances and exits, shower heads should be installed to release water so that the poison gas does not invade. However, these are all superficial lectures. To be safe, in addition to the mask, you must also wear gas protection equipment. 6. Hiding: Most people always run away when they see a dead machine. In fact, you must know that it is not as clear to look at the sky from the ground as it is to look down from a high place. Generally, aircraft flying above 6,000 feet can already see people from 11 miles away. So, if you wait until you see the aircraft to escape, it will be too late. You should escape when you hear the sound of the aircraft, otherwise you can only lie still. If you have to escape, then you can only escape to the left or right of the aircraft, because the aircraft flies in a straight line. One more thing to note is that when escaping from the aircraft, you should run along the side of the street that is not exposed to the sun.

Then, Judge Zi issued a photograph negative, which was unrelated to the bribery case, that had been found in Yang's home to Yang Chen for collection and instructed her to find the photos and invitation letters taken together by Yang and Tan and present them to the court for verification.

After leaving the institute, they will inevitably wander in the city and have no way to make a living. If they can be given appropriate education or industrial skills, they can make a living in the future. The Railway Bureau Stipulates Methods for Reporting and Transporting Less-Than-Carload Consignments of Tung Oil 125

The Railway Bureau's Traffic Department reported that the Nanchang Bridge Stationmaster had reported that customers transporting less-than-carload consignments of tung oil to Zhenjiang, Changzhou, Nanjing, and other stations used to be assembled and exported with fresh eggs from the Shangbeizhan Station. Since the implementation of direct less-than-carload consignments to Nanjing, less-than-carload consignments of tung oil have often been too small in quantity to be loaded into a separate car. They must be stored for a considerable period of time before they can be shipped, which inevitably delays the transportation of goods. It has been decided that shippers should temporarily purchase a number of sturdy oil pans to hold the tung oil in the pans so that it can be assembled into one car with dry goods. A trial run will be carried out from late February. The results of the three decisions to transport tung oil to Zhenjiang and Nanjing are very good. The Bureau has also approved the Shandong pans that have been loaded. From April 1st, following the method of transporting pigs in iron fences, the pans will be transported back to the station of origin free of charge from the station of arrival at any time.

Guangdong Rubber Company's Creditors' Meeting Yesterday 127

The company owes more than one million yuan

The reconciliation plan will be decided at the next meeting

The Shanghai Guangdong Brothers Rubber Company, since it ceased operations on November 3 last year, owes more than 1,044,000 yuan. Because it was unable to pay, it applied for understanding to the First Special District Local Court. The court accepted the case and convened the first creditors' meeting at Husheshe, Guizhou Road, yesterday afternoon at 3:00 pm to discuss the reconciliation plan. The situation is recorded as follows:

Creditors Present Yesterday's creditors present were Shanghai Electric Power Company, Jin Hongshi, Mei Zuishi Cai Binwei, Bu Naimen Ouyang Wenqiu, Silk Industry Bank, Fen Ling, Dongfang Printing House Jiang Dafu, North China Coal Industry Company Yang Zhiyi, Gao Yi Public Hall He Huiliang, Mao Sheng Electrical Materials Store Sun Zhongrong, Minsheng Company Dong Bingzhuang, Aikelong Yanghang Sun Yushu, Hefeng Qianzhuang Yu Jiaxiang, Taian Company Wang Jingsheng, and 54 other households, representing a claim of 179,486.80 yuan (the Shen Bao's claim was 470,134.65 yuan, and the registered amount was 377,011.76 yuan).

Chairman's Report The meeting was chaired by Judge Yu Lude of the First Special Court and Assistant Supervisor Accountant Li Ding. Ying Yeping, the court clerk, was the recorder. First, Judge Yu announced the purpose of the meeting, and then Accountant Li Ding reported that the total debt was 1,044,679.56 yuan and the actual value of the assets offset against the debt was 812,878.30 yuan. There were three reasons for the shutdown: A. Small capital and large scale, with no working capital in peacetime; B. No organization in accounting, so the accounts are chaotic, so the asset-liability situation cannot be expressed at any time; C. Too many borrowed funds. Based on the above reasons, the company was already in a state of financial hardship before the shutdown. However, the company's products are very suitable for the needs of modern society, so the creditors also know that the company's resumption of operations is the only hope for repaying debts.

Reconciliation Plan Then, the reconciliation plan proposed by the debtor Deng Zhaozhen was discussed. After discussion, it was decided that the plan still needed to be studied. The chairman then announced the adjournment of the meeting and waited for the decision of the second creditors' meeting. The original text of the reconciliation plan is presented below: A. All of the factory's trade names, trademarks, machinery, property, and all movable property shall be managed by the creditors providing funds within the scope of not hindering the exercise of the original powers. The method shall be in accordance with the covenant decided by the creditors. B. After the factory resumes operation, all profits from the business shall be used to repay the debts until all debts are repaid. If the creditors find that there is no profit or do not want to maintain it after accepting the management, the creditors may apply for bankruptcy. C. If the creditors cannot agree on a uniform basis, the procedure for distributing the remaining funds according to the proportion of the debt shall be as follows: the creditors who provided the funds shall be repaid the principal and interest at a monthly rate of 7% from the date of providing the funds until the date of repayment. After the above debts are repaid, 30% of the net profit shall be extracted first, with 15% being a special bonus for the creditors who provided the funds, and the remaining 15% being used to repay the old debts of the creditors who provided the funds in advance as a reward for providing the funds. The remaining 70% shall be distributed to all the creditors.

Elderly Man Falls to His Death 128

The Deceased was Yu Hongyuan, Formerly a Small Vendor

Due to Poverty and Illness Combined with His Adopted Son's Unfilial Conduct

At 11:25 PM last night, a man of about fifty years old, wearing short clothing, suddenly fell from the third floor of a certain playground in the French Concession and committed suicide. As the location was right next to the manager's office downstairs, it was immediately noticed and reported to the accounting office. Upon rushing to investigate, he was found to be already dead. After carefully examining the deceased's face, it was recognized that he was Yu Hongyuan, a local who used to work as a vendor selling items in the playground. He had a son named Xiao Fusheng, who also once worked at the playground but was later sentenced to imprisonment for a crime and is still in custody. The playground's accounting office immediately reported to the police station. The police chief ordered a detective to go to the scene for inspection and found a suicide note on the body. The wording in the letter mainly stated that he was suffering from economic hardship, was old and sickly, and his adopted son was unfilial. After the detectives completed their investigation, they immediately notified the Tongren Fuyuan branch to send undertakers to carry the body to the mortuary, pending a report requesting the Second Special Court to send personnel for an autopsy. The suicide note was kept in the police station for investigation.

City Architectural Association Releases Impressions of the Chinese Architecture Exhibition 129

Central News Agency reports that the preparation for the Chinese Architecture Exhibition has been underway for several weeks. In addition to the participation of various architectural engineering groups and individuals in the city, various material merchants have also actively participated. Moreover, telegrams from various provinces requesting to join and sending exhibits to Shanghai have been continuous, truly a grand unprecedented event in the architectural field. The Shanghai Architectural Association has published an article detailing the nature of the exhibition. It is reproduced below. Recently, Mr. Zi Gongchuo and others, in conjunction with various architectural engineering groups in the city and individuals and groups interested in architecture, initiated the Chinese Architecture Exhibition. It is scheduled to open before the opening of the Shanghai Municipal Museum, using the new building of the museum as the venue, and is scheduled to open on April 12, with the exhibition lasting for one week. In addition to the collection of architectural drawings and models by Mr. Guan Song Sheng and Mr. Zhao Shen, who are in charge from the Architectural Society of China, the Peking China Construction Society will also transport valuable items collected over the years, such as palace books, drawing plates, Song paintings, and Song tiles, to Shanghai for display. This type of architectural exhibition is still a new concept in the city. At that time, it will surely attract people from all walks of life to visit and empathize with its importance. And the greatness of the architectural industry for social culture and industry and commerce will therefore have a further understanding. The reporter is not very talented, and at the current grand event, I dare to contribute a point of view for the association to adopt. In the "National Reconstruction Program" written by the late Prime Minister Sun Yat-sen, it was stated that the construction industry is the largest enterprise in the international program. This statement is indeed true. Generally, people think that builders are all manual laborers who work hard with their hands and feet, but they do not know that builders are actually the culmination of various industries. Therefore, if you want to observe the rise and fall of a country, you must take buildings as the main material of observation. For example, archaeologists go around searching for ancient sites, all wanting to examine historical materials in broken monuments and remnant steles. Also, when we first arrive in a foreign country, we always want to see the long-standing architecture first. If our country's Peking ancient palace, Great Wall, etc., are all noted by archaeologists from various countries, and do not hesitate to travel across the ocean to visit China, those who have a biased view of the construction industry can often thoroughly understand this. And the holding of the architectural exhibition is also intended to correct the erroneous views of the general public, and to arouse attention, so that they know that architecture is closely related to housing, industry and commerce, transportation, national defense, history, and culture. This decision to hold the exhibition uses the new building of the Municipal Museum as the venue to display architectural drawings, models, calligraphy and paintings, and drawing plates. If there is not enough space, the new building of the Aviation Association can be used as the need for displaying building materials and tools. It is also learned that the municipal government will send invitations to various institutions, groups, and schools to visit at that time, so the number of people attending the meeting will be large. Therefore, the exhibits must be carefully presented. In my opinion, the display of drawings should be categorized and arranged in separate rooms. For example, for residences, Chinese style, English style, French style, American style, modern style, Spanish style, etc. should be distinguished. Also, hospitals, schools, public offices, hotels, offices, department stores, etc. should be classified and displayed according to their types. Exhibits that are not classified by type but have historical significance should be divided by era. In this way, it is orderly and the visitors can follow it. There is an indispensable display in the venue, which is the architectural system diagram. The so-called architectural system refers to the process from the architect's surveying of the construction site to the design of sketches, formal drawings, drafting of construction contracts, contracting regulations, civil engineers' plans, steel reinforcement concrete foundation and beam column roof truss and other structures, and the design of junior engineers, hot and cold water pipes, bathroom kitchen equipment, and heating and cooling settings. Also, the plans of electrical engineers, indoor lighting, electric fans, electric bells, electric heating and other devices, and the working conditions of pipeline engineers, decoration engineers, and workers in various industries, and the supply charts and explanations of various building materials, so that visitors can understand the building process of a house, which is extremely complex and not as simple as the average person imagines. In this exhibition, there are many valuable exhibits, as mentioned above, as well as the Old Summer Palace photos, models, calligraphy and paintings of the Peking Library, etc., which are all rare treasures. Therefore, compiling an exhibition journal to promote it is necessary. The journal can photograph and publish the exhibits in the exhibition, and also the preparations of the exhibition, the honorary chairman, vice chairman, and the chairman and vice chairman's inscriptions or dedications, experts' writings, the introduction of materials manufacturers' exhibits, the manufacturing process, the selection of raw materials, and the explanation of their uses, and the catalog of exhibits, etc., can be published as much as possible to promote and commemorate. However, there have been several opinions on the compilation of this booklet. Some say it should be printed together with the "Architectural Monthly," others say it should be printed together with the "Architectural Monthly" and "Chinese Architecture," and others say it should be printed independently by the association. In summary, it is appropriate to print it independently. This exhibition is still a new concept, so there must be a special publication to praise it. Although the cost is slightly higher, what harm is there? Article 5 of the Architectural Exhibition Association Charter, the scope of soliciting exhibits includes the item of soliciting tools. This will definitely arouse the interest of the visitors. The tools of each industry can be divided into two types: manual and machine. If the brick and tile workers use machines to mix mud, make blanks, and fire them, compared with using manpower or ox power to mix mud, manually make blanks, and fire in earth kilns, and woodworkers use spring saws to saw large sections of wood into boards, then use circular saws to saw into strips, and then use cut-off saws to saw into short sections, after which they use hand planes to polish them, one side at a time, flat planers to roll them flat, line planing machines to plane lines, foot chiseling machines, barrel head machines, gluing machines and other abutting actions, and stone machines to split stone, grind stone, cut edges, and iron machines to plane, drill, turn, rivet, weld, paint acid brushing, spraying, dipping and other processes, so that visitors to the exhibition can visit several factories at the same time. In this short period of time, it is practically impossible to arrange so many machines and tools, or to omit machine tools and only display hand tools, which will not arouse the attention of the general public. Therefore, the item of tools can be temporarily omitted due to circumstances, and preparations should be made early for the next exhibition to achieve perfection. However, it is not appropriate to give up eating because of choking, and the remedy is to ask building material merchants to take photos or display real objects of raw materials, manufacturing methods, and tools when displaying their products, and add explanations. This is better than nothing. The architectural exhibition is intended to arouse the attention of the general public, so it is feared that simply displaying drawings will not be fully understood. It is best to make more models. Among the eastern styles, Indian, Japanese, architectural carvings and paintings, and the architecture of the Near East, Egypt, Syria, Syria, Persia, and the Western classic, revival, and Greek Roman transformed styles from Britain, France, Germany, etc., select the whole and reduce it by several times in scale, or select the parts and make models of plaster or lime in the same scale, and add explanations to each part and the process of historical transformation. Also, famous buildings in our country's history, such as Epang Palace and Deer Terrace, can also refer to ancient books, plan drawings, and make models, and go to the sites to excavate, or may be able to dig up broken bricks and tiles for the exhibition, which will also be of great benefit to our country's archaeology. According to this search, after several years of effort, the historical materials of architectural history will also be greatly supplemented. Our country is known as an ancient country with 5,000 years of culture, but the history of architecture is still lacking, which is really embarrassing. Therefore, architects who are directly responsible for this task should rise up and catch up, and continue to move forward after this exhibition in order to implement their responsibilities. The Chinese Architecture Exhibition should still be retained after the exhibition is over, and the municipal government should be requested to allocate land and funding in the city center to build a venue and establish an architectural museum, and continue to manufacture models and other exhibits, and collect historical materials on architecture, then the importance of this museum will not be less than that of the library and museum. Shanghai is a gathering place for Chinese and foreign people, and international visitors will come in droves. Those who first set foot on this land are shocked that this is not the Shanghai of the East. To correct this view, it is necessary to visit the city center and the various departments of the architectural museum to make them appreciate the greatness of Chinese culture and gain a good international impression. Therefore, the establishment of an architectural museum is also an urgent matter.

"Healthy World Monthly" Sells Well 130

Since its launch, the "Healthy World Monthly," though not long in existence, has achieved great success and is highly praised. The reason is that the publication combines the strengths of pictorials, hygiene, sports, medicine, bodybuilding, martial arts, and literature into one. Therefore, its posture is unique, and it spares no effort in imparting health knowledge, so that outsiders can roughly know the way to health and strengthening the body, and insiders can learn from each other on pharmacology and pathology. The content is exceptionally rich, with more than sixty pages in each issue. The price is extremely low, and the retail price is six cents per copy, including postage. The annual subscription for twelve issues is fifty cents in domestic currency, including postage in China, eighty cents in Hong Kong and Macau, and one dollar in Europe, America, and Southeast Asia. It has now been published to the fifth issue. Recently, the Healthy World Society at No. 14, Lane 214, Tongfu Road, Shanghai, has received more than one hundred letters a day, and many people have also attached two and a half cents to buy back issues one, two, three, and four. It is also heard that the publication is sold at the local Life Bookstore and major newsstands.

Overview of the Organizational Structure of Shanghai Grain Merchant Groups (3) (19th Overview of Shanghai Industry and Commerce) 134

— Compiled by China Credit

3. Commercial Group Organizations of the Miscellaneous Grain and Oilseed Cake Industry

1. Shanghai Miscellaneous Grain and Oilseed Cake Trade Association. This association is abbreviated as the Miscellaneous Grain Association. Its address is No. 312, Minguo Wai Road, Xinbeimen. It was founded in the ninth year of the Republic of China. At the beginning of the organization, the soybean and rice industry's prestigious figures concurrently served as the directors of the association. The first president was Mr. Ye Huijun. In addition, vice presidents and directors were elected from the Hakka community. Later, the president system was changed to a committee system, and the current chairman of the committee is also Mr. Gu Shengyi. Since its establishment, although it has only a history of thirteen years, it has been the most powerful among the rising forces. Its members are based on the soybean and rice industry, accounting for more than half of all members. It is said that the association was transformed from a tea party of the soybean and rice industry's Bianji Hakka community before the ninth year of the Republic of China. At the beginning, it was stipulated that it should be jointly established by Chinese merchants operating miscellaneous grains, oil, soybeans, and cakes in Shanghai, so it was originally named the Shanghai Chinese Merchants Miscellaneous Grain, Oil, Soybean, and Cake Trade Association. Internally, it is divided into six Hakka communities, totaling seven guild halls. The list is as follows:

1. Local Merchants Guild Hall: Cuixiu Guild Hall (Soybean Industry)

2. Local Merchants Guild Hall: Rengu Guild Hall (Rice Industry)

3. Han Hakka (Zhicheng Guild Hall). The so-called Han Hakka does not refer to Hankou merchants traveling in Shanghai, but actually refers to merchants specializing in miscellaneous grains, soybeans, and rice between Hankou and the upper reaches of the Yangtze River and Shanghai, most of whom are Ningbo people from Zhejiang.

Zhenjiang Hakka: Jiyuantang Guild Hall. The capital of the various merchants of this Hakka is strong, and their business is developed. In addition to miscellaneous grains, they also deal in northern and southern grains and groceries. They are now also basic members of the Miscellaneous Grain Association. However, at that time, this Hakka did not have a formal organization established, but was affiliated with the Zhicheng Guild Hall.

4. Guangdong Hakka: Shenshou Guild Hall. This is organized by Guangzhou grain merchants in Shanghai and is affiliated with the Guangzhao Guild Hall.

5. Chaozhou Hakka: Chaozhou Sugar and Grocery Federation. This is organized by Chaozhou merchants in Shanghai and is different from Shenshou Hall. The business of this Hakka is not limited to miscellaneous grains, so it joins under the name of the Sugar and Grocery Federation.

6. Fujian Hakka: Sanshan Guild Hall. Also known as Fuzhou Hakka, it is organized by Fuzhou merchants in Shanghai. The scope of business operations of people from Fujian Province is also broad, and the miscellaneous grain industry is one part of the Sanshan Guild Hall.

7. Xiamen Hakka: Quanzhang Guild Hall. It is organized by Xiamen merchants in Shanghai, and the grain industry is only one part of it. After the eighteenth year of the Republic of China, various industries in Shanghai were reorganized. The association also changed its name to the Shanghai Miscellaneous Grain and Oilseed Cake Trade Association because the original name seemed to conflict with the soybeans of the soybean and rice industry. At first, it was collected in the name of various Hakkas, with the business as the main body, so it was called member business. Now, it does not list Hakka affiliation, but only lists the representatives of the business. However, its content is still the previous Hakkas, but the soybean and rice industries have been merged, and the Zhenjiang Hakka has independently organized.

Businesses that specialize in or concurrently deal in miscellaneous grains and oil cakes do not completely join the public food industry. Even in terms of Hakka groups, there are still the Jiangxi Hakka Jiyi Tang Guild Hall and the Tianjin Hakka Shunzhi Guild Hall, which have not joined. Other Hakkas from various provinces and cities such as Shantou, Quanzhou, Yantai, Longkou, Haizhou, Qingdao, Yingkou, Hunan, Sichuan, Dalian, and Anhui have also not joined. Foreign merchants who specialize in the import and export of miscellaneous grains, rice, wheat flour, and bran, although some of them, such as British and Japanese firms, also have great influence and have frequent dealings with Chinese merchants, they all trade in the name of foreign firms or individuals. They have their own commercial organizations, so they do not join Chinese commercial organizations.

2. Shanghai Miscellaneous Grain Retail Trade Association. This is jointly organized by retail miscellaneous grain stores and a part of brokers. It specializes in selling by the "dou" measure and does not engage in wholesale, which is similar to the Rice Number Trade Association of the rice industry. The scope of this industry is smaller than rice stores, and it is often concurrently operated by rice stores. It was founded in the tenth year of the Republic of China and has many members, but they are very scattered. The address is No. 2, Cuifeng Lane, Doushi Street. The current chairman of the committee is Mr. Sun Jiaoyun.

3. Shanghai Grain, Miscellaneous Oil, and Cake Exchange Broker Association. This association is a combination of the same nature as the Flour Exchange Broker Association, that is, the group of brokers in the Miscellaneous Grain Exchange. The quota of brokers in the exchange is 100, which is more than flour brokers; but in fact, it is not full. The Miscellaneous Grain Exchange was founded by soybean, rice, and miscellaneous grain merchants, and brokers are also mostly filled by soybean, rice, and miscellaneous grain merchants, so it seems to be more stable than flour brokers. However, its business is not very developed, and its activity has been far less than that of flour brokers in recent years. The current chairman and vice chairman of the committee are Mr. Chuan Changyu and Mr. Xue Chengzhang. The members, trainees, staff, and workers of the Miscellaneous Grain and Oilseed Cake Exchange have also organized the Shanghai Miscellaneous Grain and Oilseed Cake Exchange Trade Union. This association is similar to the Flour Exchange Staff Association; but this one has a wider range of workers and has survived until now after several reorganizations. Its organization is in accordance with trade union regulations, so it is of a trade union nature rather than a commercial combination.

4. Shanghai Oil Mill Trade Association. This association is the Oil Mill Association, which is organized by various machine oil mills. However, there are very few oil mills in Shanghai, and the organization of the products is neither as grand and rigorous as the various factories in the Northeast, nor as numerous as the inland oil workshops. The raw materials for oil production are soybeans, floral cores, and peanuts, rapeseed, etc. are also often used. Among them, the operators are divided into Guangdong Hakka and Zhejiang Hakka. Common products on the market, such as soybean oil, raw oil (peanut oil), clear oil (floral core oil), as well as soybean cakes, floral cakes, peanut cakes, etc., are mostly produced by Lide, Dayou, Dachang, Feng, Dadexin, Shenghelong, and Juchanghe factories. Rapeseed oil and rapeseed cakes are mostly manufactured by inland workshops, and Shanghai factories do not pay attention to them. Sesame oil is made by small grinders, and factories have gradually paid attention to this recently. The address is No. 105, Jiangxi Road, and the current chairman of the committee is Mr. Zhu Jingan.

Education News

Ministry of Education Orders Vocational Schools to Focus on Off-Campus Internships and Cooperate with Construction Agencies 135

(Nanjing, 26th) The Ministry of Education ordered the education administrative agencies of various provinces and cities that the Ministry has found that the knowledge and skills learned by graduates of various provincial industrial schools at school do not fully meet the needs of actual work, making it difficult to gain the trust of the industry. The reason is that the teaching curriculum of vocational schools still needs to be improved, and the internship equipment is not perfect, resulting in various work skills being impure, and the lack of off-campus internship opportunities. Students cannot have full contact with the industry, which is the biggest problem. In addition to repeatedly sending personnel to inspect and guide, and ordering to increase funding to enrich equipment and improve teaching, the Executive Yuan has also approved orders to various ministries, committees, departments, provincial and municipal governments, and sub-messages to the National Economic Commission, etc., to instruct industrial, commercial, health, transportation and other construction agencies to allow vocational school students of the same nature to practice as much as possible. On the one hand, vocational school students can gain practical experience and increase work efficiency, and on the other hand, they can communicate supply and demand needs and cultivate talents suitable for social production. Five guidelines for cooperation between vocational schools and construction agencies have been formulated. You are instructed to order the public and private vocational schools under your jurisdiction to discuss with the construction agencies of the same nature as the school and draw up detailed off-campus internship measures for students. Report to the office for approval and implementation, and at the end of each semester, compile and summarize the internship overview of each school and report to the department for review.
