Points for Improvement in Sichuan Education: Report of Chen Lijiang's Inspection 137

Chen Lijiang has returned from his inspection of education in Sichuan Province. His impressions of the inspection were briefly reported in this newspaper. Now, the Ministry of Education has released a formal report, instructing the Sichuan Provincial Department of Education as follows: "According to the report on his inspection of education in the province submitted by Chen Lijiang, Special Inspector of the Ministry, it has been reviewed and the points requiring improvement in the province are hereby printed and shown as follows:"

1. Regarding Elementary School Education: (1) The existing number of elementary schools in the province has not yet been statistically determined. The department should promptly investigate the current status of elementary schools throughout the province, compile statistics on elementary schools throughout the province, and formulate a multi-year plan as the basis for improvement. (2) The six-year elementary schools in the province are mostly concentrated in cities. Rural elementary schools are all single-level or complexly structured primary elementary schools. For the sake of balanced development of urban and rural elementary schools, the department should immediately close elementary schools in cities with few graduates and relocate them to rural areas, or use county funds to operate or subsidize rural elementary schools. (3) The province and each county and city should organize elementary education research associations and use winter and summer vacations to hold elementary school teacher training courses. The department should also hire elementary education experts and implement a guidance system to improve the qualifications of elementary school teachers. (4) Most elementary schools in the province start in the spring, but the textbooks used are for the autumn semester. The content of the teaching materials is often inconsistent with the seasons. The starting class in spring should be gradually changed to the starting class in autumn, or books for the starting class in spring should be used. (5) Provincial elementary schools should be opened in Wanxian, Chongqing, Jiading, and Ya'an as a model for nearby counties to improve their elementary schools. Chongqing is densely populated, and the existing elementary schools are insufficient. The city should properly raise funds and build more elementary schools. (6) For the purpose of improving elementary school education in Sichuan, the newly established Provincial Chengdu Experimental Elementary School should be expanded and conduct serious experiments. In accordance with previous orders, the school should jointly lead the improvement of elementary education in Sichuan Province with the Chongqing Private Bashu Elementary School. At the same time, elementary school teachers throughout the province should be ordered to visit and learn from it in order to achieve the effect of observation.

2. Regarding Compulsory Education: (1) Only half of the counties and cities in the province have established short-term elementary schools. Those that have not yet been established should be ordered to open them immediately to comply with the regulations. (2) The department should instruct all counties and cities to make the promotion of compulsory education and the establishment of short-term elementary schools the central task of educational administration and actively carry it out. (3) The should quickly dispatch provincial inspectors, etc., to guide and supervise the counties and cities, and assess their performance. (4) The department should inform all counties and cities that the funds for short-term elementary schools that have been included in the budget must be properly raised, sources must be determined, and they must be disbursed on schedule. (5) The 140,000 yuan in initial assistance funds allocated to the province by the central government and the 150,000 yuan in subsidies allocated by the provincial government should be quickly allocated and distributed to the counties and cities on a monthly basis to facilitate the process. (6) Chongqing has a dense population and many out-of-school children. The city should be ordered to open the planned short-term elementary schools as soon as possible. Regarding funding, the city should quickly raise funds. If there are insufficient funds, subsidies should be considered.

3. Regarding Secondary Schools and Normal Education: (1) Jointly established secondary schools in the province should be considered for transfer to provincial management. There are too many county-established secondary schools. They should be appropriately merged or converted into normal schools or vocational schools. (2) Private secondary schools in the province urgently need to be reorganized. The Department of Education must formulate specific measures for implementation and formulate measures to subsidize excellent private secondary schools in order to encourage them. (3) The Department of Education should immediately organize a provincial secondary school building and equipment management committee. Its functions are to design and determine the construction plan of secondary schools throughout the province and promote its implementation, as well as to unify the investigation and purchase of equipment in secondary schools, with the goal of starting, supervising, and improving in the near future. (4) For secondary schools and normal schools, if the ratio of full-time to part-time teachers does not meet the regulations, it should be corrected immediately. The list of faculty and staff of each school should be prepared by the principal from qualified personnel and submitted to the Education Department for approval, and then the principal should hire them. (5) Secondary schools and normal schools should strictly abide by the course standards and revised timetable promulgated by the Ministry of Education. They must not arbitrarily add or subtract subjects or increase or decrease class hours. (6) Science experiments should be supervised by teachers and students should do it themselves and submit a detailed report. (7) There is no need to set up checkers at the school exits. Detailed measures should be formulated for students entering and leaving the school based on the situation of boarding and commuting, and strictly enforced by the training staff. (8) The should divide the province into normal school districts, make overall plans to train teachers for moral education, and should set up a provincial rural normal school with an experimental area for rural education. (9) The buildings of the Provincial Chongqing Women's Normal School are narrow and urgently need to be rebuilt or relocated. (10) Female teachers should be employed more in women's normal schools. (11) More time should be given to teaching practice, and its implementation should be supervised. (12) Full-time teachers should live in the school to effectively manage it.

4. Regarding Vocational Education: (1) The province should follow the regulations of the "Ministry's Standards for the Establishment and Funding Distribution of Secondary Schools" when conducting vocational education, distributing ratios, and based on the province's economic construction situation, hire experts to organize a vocational education design committee to formulate a detailed plan for the future development of vocational education. (2) Most of the existing vocational schools are concentrated in Chengdu and Chongqing. Future expansions should pay attention to popularizing them throughout the province. (3) The equipment in each school is still too simple. The expense should be increased in accordance with the provisions of Article 20 of the Revised Vocational School Regulations. (4) Each school should have a director of practice. Experienced technicians should be hired for each subject to provide practical guidance, and the practice time should be increased. (5) Each school should strive to closely connect with industrial institutions and allow students to practice in the field. (6) In addition to learning agricultural technology, agricultural students should also pay attention to rural economic knowledge, such as cooperatives, warehouse management, and rural loans. (7) There are too many part-time teachers in each school, and strict orders should be given to improve this. (8) The majors in the Provincial Chengdu and Chongqing Women's Vocational Schools are too mixed and should be reorganized immediately. (9) Each school should be equipped with vocational supplementary schools or vocational training classes that meet local needs. The above points must be followed and improved, and the handling situation should be reported for future reference. This order.

Health Education Association Reorganized and Established in This City 140

Presiding Over Professional Health Education in the City

Nanjing City Collects Hygiene Fees

The Health Education Committee of this city held a reorganization and establishment conference at the Health Bureau conference room yesterday morning at 10:00 a.m. Committee members Pan Gongzhan (represented by Li), Li Ting'an, Zeng Shengdian, Jiang Jianbai, Chen Bai, Hu Shuhao, Zhang Yongchun, Zhou Peicheng, Shao Rugan, Wu Liguo, Wang Shiwei, Ma Gan, You Jihua, and Zhao Zuan attended. Chen Bai, Hu Shuyi, Zhang Yongchun, and six others were elected to draft regulations and methods, which will be convened by Hu Shu and completed within two weeks. In imitation of Nanjing's collection of health fees, the method will also be planned by the above-mentioned six committee members. The business plan will be discussed at the second meeting after the regulations are drafted. At noon, Director Pan hosted a lunch at the city government cooperative.

Sports News: Our Country's Davis Cup Representative, Mr. Xu Chengji, Departed the Country Yesterday Afternoon

Lin Baohua and his wife traveled with him. Cai Huiquan boarded the ship in Hong Kong. The Davis Cup Preliminary Round will Begin on May 5th, with the First Encounter Being France.

For the 1936 Davis Cup International Tennis Tournament, after our country decided to appoint Mr. Xu Chengji and Zheng Zhaojia as representatives, Zheng went directly to Paris across the Atlantic from the United States. Xu arrived in Shanghai from Hong Kong on the 12th of this month and defeated the local Western star Carson twice with scores of three to one and three to zero. He departed the country yesterday afternoon at 11:00 a.m. with Mr. and Mrs. Lin Baohua, former representatives of our country's Davis Cup, who are going to France at their own expense. Those who saw him off included Mrs. Tan Lao and Lin Xianjin. The details are as follows:

Our Country Joins the European Zone

According to Mr. Xu, the number of countries participating in the Davis Cup in the previous session reached thirty units, while in this session there were only twenty-three countries. There are fifteen countries participating in the European zone. In fact, there are only four countries competing in the American zone. Our country used to join the American zone and has now entered the European zone at the same time as Argentina. Because of the Davis Cup rules, any country can freely participate in the European and American zones without absolute restrictions. The preliminary selection has now been abolished, which has indeed made it easier for most countries. However, Japan, South Africa, New Zealand, and Italy have stopped attending for various reasons, reducing the interest. Among the nineteen countries participating in the European zone, Germany and the Czech Republic have been the most promising in the past. The results of the competition will likely form a three-way situation. The drawing ceremony for the Davis Cup tennis in this session was held on February 3 at the Egyptian Pavilion of the Earl of Ho's residence in London, hosted by London Mayor Vincent De, and was extremely grand.

Our Country's First Battle Is Against France

As a result of the draw, the first week of byes and matches will be Morocco, the Netherlands, China, France, Spain, and Germany. The remaining Argentina, Sweden, Switzerland, Denmark, Norway, Greece, Hungary, Poland, Romania, Yugoslavia, and Ireland will all have byes. The match dates will be the first week starting on May 5, the second week on May 17, the third week on June 9, and the fourth week on June 19. The European Zone finals will be on July 13, and the Inter-Zone will be on July 18, 20, and 21 for three days. The championship will be held in Wimbledon on July 25, 27, and 28 for three days. The order of the first and second weeks is as follows:

Cai Huiquan Leaves Hong Kong for a Stopover Tomorrow

Xu continued, "This time I was sent to Europe. As a result of the draw, unfortunately, we first encountered France, which is a great pity. England and France are the hegemons in the European zone. Although France has not won the Inter-Zone finals for two years, the male phoenix still exists. Moreover, the English general Pan Lai was injured in the shoulder when he attended the singles championship finals last year, and it has become increasingly serious recently. Even a slight gesture is inconvenient, which gives France a great opportunity. France will not easily let go of this opportunity, so it makes myself and Mr. Zheng even more difficult. However, we are not discouraged and will continue to work hard to repay our countrymen. Mr. Cai Huiquan returned to Hong Kong the day before yesterday to take care of personal matters and is scheduled to board a ship in Hong Kong tomorrow to meet with Mr. and Mrs. Lin Shihua and myself on the same boat to Europe. Mr. Zheng Zhaojia telegraphed the other day, saying that he would depart from the United States in about a week, cross the Atlantic, and meet in Paris in mid-May."

School Survey

Overview of the Shanghai American School (3) 150

— Hu Zuyin

4. Teaching and Moral Education

One aspect of teaching worth mentioning is that the school has established minimum standards for the academic level of students in each grade. This allows both teachers and students to strive towards these standards. Now, let me introduce the minimum standards for the Chinese and arithmetic subjects for the first and sixth grades of the school's elementary school for reference.

Minimum Standards for Chinese and Arithmetic in the First Grade of Elementary School

Chinese: 1. Reading:

Able to read and understand the texts in the first-grade textbook.

Able to express the meaning of the read text using their own language, actions, drawings, or collages.

Able to understand simple instructions on the blackboard or in the composition textbook.

Able to pronounce clearly without stuttering.

Able to recognize new characters using the following four methods:

(1) Pictures

(2) Association of ideas

(3) Pronunciation

(4) Asking the teacher

Able to read without pointing fingers.

Has read five or more books from the library.

Familiar with 500 characters from the commonly used character list and able to recite 150 characters.

2. Spelling:

Able to spell 35 basic characters.

Able to attempt to spell new characters other than the 35 basic characters.

3. Language:

When talking, able to wait for others to finish speaking before speaking, and able to listen to others politely.

Speaks clearly and distinctly.

Able to express meaning using complete sentences when necessary.

Able to use capital letters for: proper nouns; the first word in a sentence; and the word "I".

Able to use a period at the end of each sentence.

Able to write one or two sentences from a story.

Able to recite ten short poems in a year.

4. Writing:

Understands how to write each letter.

Able to hold the pencil correctly and have good writing posture.

Able to find ways to improve writing skills.

Arithmetic:

Able to count one by one, five by five, and ten by ten, from one to one hundred.

Able to count two by two, from one to twenty-four.

Able to write one by one, five by five, and ten by ten, from one to one hundred.

Able to express time using hours or half hours.

Understands the meaning of half, quarter; one inch, one foot, one yard; one dozen, half a dozen.

Able to read and find the page numbers in the textbook.

Understands the twenty-four facts that must be known in addition.

Understands the meaning of "take away."

Minimum Standards for Chinese and Arithmetic in the Sixth Grade of Elementary School

Chinese: 1. Grammar:

Achieve the reading level of the sixth grade based on the standard reading test.

Able to read silently at least 185 words from the sixth-grade textbook in one minute and understand them.

Able to read aloud clearly to others.

Able to write an outline of the reading material.

Has read ten books from the library in a year and made reports.

2. Spelling:

Able to use a dictionary to check new characters.

Able to have independent spelling methods.

Does not make careless spelling errors in writing other work reports.

Able to spell the new characters in the sixth-grade basic character list, and able to achieve 80% accuracy.

Cotton Yarn Prices Soar 151

—Spot and Forward Prices All Exceed Fifty Dollars—

The cotton market has soared, and the situation is unusually firm. This is because cotton inventories are low, and financial firms and banks have uniformly closed off a large amount of spot cotton. The Japanese firm, Toyo Cotton Company, also took in more than 10,000 piculs of March cotton. Spot and forward cotton prices are all rising rapidly.

Open Flower Closing Jumps Sharply

The opening market for open flower futures saw increases across all months. Because the bulls in the near months were rumored to have organized a company to prepare for a squeeze, buying was especially strong, and the upward momentum was particularly intense. Aiji also came in to drag up prices. However, U.S. cotton rose by one to eight points, and Indian cotton fell by 0.5 to 2 rupees due to sales by European exporters. Nevertheless, market buyers were enthusiastic. As a result, all months rose by 3, 4, and 5 jiao compared to the previous day's closing price. The afternoon opening market situation was extremely sharp. The availability of chips was very scarce. There were rumors of bullish news. Tongji continued to absorb cotton, and the price increase became even more intense. By closing, the far months were jumping 3 jiao, and all months had risen beyond the $5 mark. As a result, all months rose by 2, 3, 4, and 5 jiao compared to the morning closing price. Sales included 1,600 piculs by Xiesheng, 3,500 piculs by Dafu, 3,900 piculs by Jinchang, 2,500 piculs by Senkang, 2,700 piculs by Changfeng, 1,100 piculs by Yikang, 1,300 piculs by Ruiyuan, 1,600 piculs by Dafeng, 2,900 piculs by Daji, 1,700 piculs by Yuanyi, and 2,000 piculs by Hengchang. Purchases included 1,100 piculs by Yichang, 1,200 piculs by Runkang, 2,400 piculs by Hexing, 1,900 piculs by Jifeng, 2,600 piculs by Meiji, 4,000 piculs by Tongji, 1,600 piculs by Gengfeng, 2,000 piculs by Shengyuan, 3,000 piculs by Changhe, 3,300 piculs by Yuda, and 2,300 piculs by Mingde. Yarn Market Follows Raw Cotton Upward 152

—August Futures Re-emerge Above the $210 Mark—

The yarn market, which had been weak for four days in a row, suddenly reported an increase today. This was truly due to relaxed financing and the firm intention of the banking sector to absorb supply. Yesterday, the sellers of the March futures were delivering cotton, which was fully accepted by the buyers. At the same time, raw cotton prices jumped, causing the bullish trend in the market to reignite. August futures re-emerged above the $210 mark. If customer sales can continue to come in, the future outlook is certainly optimistic.

Tense Atmosphere in the Spun Yarn Market

The opening market for spun yarn futures saw a gradual rise in all months. Although the sellers were under pressure to deliver yesterday, the financial sector fully accepted the deliveries, and market sentiment saw a turnaround. Sellers were scarce, and the market price gradually rose. As a result, all months rose by 9 jiao to 1 yuan and 1 jiao compared to the previous day's closing price. In the afternoon opening market, the sentiment remained tense. The trading floor felt particularly dry. This was because Hexing came in to make a large amount of offsetting purchases. The market price moved forward steadily. This was truly because the soaring cotton market dragged the interdependent yarn market into a better situation. As a result, all months continued to rise by 3, 4, and 6 jiao compared to the morning closing price. Sales included 650 bales by Deda, 1,200 bales by Dafu, 500 bales by Yuda, 2,050 bales by Daji, 1,000 bales by Jinchang, 1,150 bales by Senkang, 450 bales by Yichang, and 400 bales by Yongchang. Food: Rumors of Conflict Between Japan and Russia, Flour and Wheat Suddenly Rebound 155

Flour: Yesterday, when the flour market opened in the morning, the market for each month showed a phenomenon of initially being flat and then jumping sharply. The quoted price of foreign wheat was around two jiao lower in Chicago and four or eight cents lower in Canada. When the price was opened, due to the good weather, although market sentiment was weak, because the factory did not hedge and many outsiders were long, the distant futures had fallen nearly two jiao from the highest level of the previous week, so buying was strong. The market gradually rose steadily. When the market opened in the afternoon, the market for each month suddenly turned tight, and the price rose quite quickly. Due to rumors of conflict between Japan and Russia and various domestic circumstances, the attention of the bulls was aroused. Near-term contracts rose by two cents, while far-term contracts rose by three or four cents. It is feared that the potential for speculation will grow, leading to unpredictable situations.

Wheat: Yesterday, the wheat market was flat to steady in the morning after opening, and then expensive in the afternoon. Initially, the weather was clear, and the opening price was similar to the previous one. Later, the flour market turned firm, and prices rose by two or three cents. When the market opened in the afternoon, there were not many transactions in the current month, and it remained stable. Distant futures were shaken by rumors in the market, and short positions became restrained. The opening price rose step by step, reversing up by seven or nine cents to one jiao compared to the previous day. Industry insiders speculate that because the current price difference between old and new wheat is around one yuan, outside buyers may be using this as a ratio, so future changes cannot be predicted for the time being. The spot wheat market remains stable. The opening price of Yao Bay Suqian wheat was $5.32, with over a thousand bags taken by Fuxin.

It is speculated that the overseas wheat market harvest this year will reach 800 million bushels. The meteorological station predicts that the southwest weather will continue to improve. The bulls are very disappointed. The stomach of the flour mills is not healthy, causing market sentiment to be difficult to revitalize.

Hankou Tung Oil Surges for Days - Foreign Firms Replenish Orders, Market Price Rises by Ten Yuan - Zhejiang Tung Follows Suit, Shanghai Market Situation Tightens

Since the beginning of the month, when Hankou white tung oil began to be sought after by foreign firms, the market has gradually soared. Prices stabilized around mid-month after most firms had completed their purchases for the month. Unexpectedly, a significant amount for April remained unfulfilled. The foreign firms initially anticipated abundant supply as spring approached and the river waters rose. However, the Yangtze River upstream remained shallow, causing significant delays in water transport. Arrivals in Hankou dwindled, and with delivery deadlines approaching, firms were compelled to bid up prices. Demand far exceeded supply, becoming increasingly apparent. In the past week, foreign firms in Hankou have been scouring the market, willing to pay any price to secure available stock. The market has witnessed a surge, with prices rising from 62-63 yuan per dan daily, escalating multiple times each day. This week, prices have reached 66.5 yuan. In the last two or three days, the price increase has intensified. Two days ago, the price stood at 68.5 yuan, but yesterday's telegram reported a rise to 71 yuan, and today's telegram indicates 73.5 yuan, with the situation remaining tight. In just ten days, the price has risen by more than ten yuan, which is quite alarming. However, the situation has yet to stabilize, and it is possible that prices may reach 80 yuan in the near future. Rumors suggest that Hankou foreign firms have a shortage of two to three thousand tons for April delivery, which must be fully replenished before mid-April, resulting in a critical shortage of spot goods. From the reporter's observations, the price surge is entirely driven by speculative buying. Once the frenzy subsides, there may be a period of consolidation, but with the base price now high, any correction is unlikely to be excessive. For the past two months, Zhejiang tung oil has been cheaper than Hankou tung oil. With the surge in Hankou tung oil prices, Zhejiang tung oil has followed suit. Yesterday, the market price for Zhejiang tung oil for Jiangxi delivery was 70 yuan per *chu*, and most local export merchants found it difficult to secure stock, making the situation even more tense than in Hankou.

6. Cash Reserve and Silver Movement

The inventory of Shanghai Chinese and foreign banks has averaged over 400 million yuan per month since September of the 21st year of the Republic. As mentioned in Section 2 of this article, the reason why the call loan market was weak in the three years prior to the 23rd year of the Republic, averaging no more than 10 cents or more per month (see the Shanghai Call Rate Fluctuation Table), was due to the excessive abundance of silver reserves. However, starting in August of the 23rd year of the Republic, influenced by the American silver policy, cash outflow was rampant, and inventories decreased monthly. The total average at the end of the 23rd year of the Republic was 502.773 million yuan. In January of last year, the total inventory was only 335.08 million yuan, a decrease of over 167 million yuan. Therefore, the emptiness of Shanghai's inventory last year was unseen in the past five or six years. The monthly total was always below 330 million yuan, never exceeding this number. This is the source of the tight money supply and credit contraction. See the table below. Shen Bao Literary Supplement

On the Hu Zhongzao Poetry Case 173

— Tang Tao

I once wrote an article called "Literary Inquisition," which involved Hu Zhongzao. I believed that Hu was a thoroughgoing slave and would never harbor ethnic prejudices. Later, I saw another article on the same topic. The author believed that although Hu Zhongzao did not have "ethnic color," his poems "had quite a bit of anti-Qing thought and mocked and cursed wonderfully." He cited poems such as "The Qing wind does not know words, why does it turn the books in disorder?" "The Ming Dynasty will spread its wings and fly to Qingdu in one fell swoop," and "I see the Emperor of the Great Ming today, let's put Hu'er aside for now."

Hu Zhongzao's *Jianmo Sheng Poetry Collection* is probably impossible to find now, so we have no way of knowing the facts inside. However, from the imperial edicts of the Qianlong Emperor, we can still see the excerpted verses. The first thing that Qianlong considered rebellious was the book title, saying: "Jianmo comes from the Analects of Confucius, and the grinding mentioned by Confucius refers to Buddhism. Hu Zhongzao uses this as his title, what is his intention!" As for the excerpted verses, I will now copy them below and briefly explain the reasons why Qianlong considered them rebellious.

(1) "A world without sun and moon," "Also descend a world of spring, summer, autumn, and winter" -- Qianlong believed that since the Qing Dynasty established its rule, it has been peaceful and prosperous, far surpassing the Han, Tang, Song, and Ming dynasties. To say that another world has descended shows a lack of human heart.

(2) "A handful of heart to discuss turbidity Qing" -- putting the word "turbid" on the dynastic title.

(3) "Heaven did not open Qingtai," "Civilization wants to be covered by barbarians," "Please look at all Angbei when we meet, who knows that the beauty belongs to the fur-clad people?" -- pointing out that he picked at the differences between Han and Manchu.

(4) "The Southern Dipper sends me south, the Northern Dipper sends me north, the space between the Southern and Northern Dippers is not even a millet wide," "Sail again across the Xiang River towards the North Sea, look closely at how it came to be," "Intend to unveil the Northern Dipper, angrily exhaust the southern wind," "Temporarily rest the southern wind" -- criticizing him for repeatedly separating the north and south.

(5) "Emperor Mu of the Zhou Dynasty, his carriages and horses never stopped," "Emperor Wu lost his city for beauty," "White snow is difficult to harmonize, a single word of praise cannot be added" -- because the wording and allusions used were irrelevant to the poem's topic, pointing out that it contained malicious satire.

(6) "Old Buddha has no illness now, but the court hears that the gate is not open" -- spreading rumors.

(7) "Is there no vital energy in the world?" "Not for sightseeing indulge the thieves," "After the three talents are born, there is today" -- the meaning of the words is rebellious.

(8) "The heaven that is illuminated is all sun and moon, the earth has no way to measure west and east, all the dukes of the Five Mountains, all the dukes of rivers, have been similar in the past hundred years," "King Zhou only goes according to the times" -- the former implies that the mountains and rivers are ashamed, the latter uses the story of King Zhao's southern expedition, with malicious satire.

(9) "Also the son of heaven, also wearing Laiyi," "Now it is also a Tushan meeting, and the jade and silk are ten times more" -- the three "also" words are "extremely disrespectful."

(10) "Blue flies throw themselves into the dung, how can they refuse to speak?" "That is a partial disaster and rain is falling now, just like the Buddha lighting lamps on weekdays" -- the first sentence mocks listening to slanderous words, and the last two sentences mock not providing disaster relief.

(11) "Beside the flowers, I feel that a single flower has no stalk," "Her husband is my father, and his wife is also the way of the mother," "The female ruler and the ruler are one body, how can it be as deep as Ao?" -- These poems are about the death of Empress Xiaoxian. To the emperor and empress, he directly calls them "her husband" and "his wife," and the term "ruler and father" is a common title for people. The ruler is more honorable than the father, but Hu's poem compares the ruler to the father, so he is mentally deranged.

(12) "To be spared my crown is to come out," "Who can perfect the rough jade in one lifetime? I fear that my body's pot will break," "If I can be the master, I will only break free from the reins," "A lifetime is as dizzy as a bird in a cage," "I would be ashamed of being a louse official," "Heaven is only to ask me about provincial affairs," "Today I am afraid to catch the wind," "Sneakily shoot stingrays with sand, greedy wolves spread their wings" -- These are all words of complaint.

The above-quoted poems were excerpted by Qianlong from Hu Zhongzao's *Jianmo Sheng Poetry Collection*, and they are the rebellious evidence that led to Hu Zhongzao's execution. However, in my opinion, Hu Zhongzao not only had no ethnic prejudices but also had no satire that could be accepted. Some of his verses were intended to show off his talent, deliberately using a few dangerous rhymes, obscure allusions, and irrelevant insertions; some were deliberately complaining, as if his great talent was being buried. As for the lines "Civilization wants to be covered by barbarians," "Who knows that the beauty belongs to the fur-clad people?" I suspect that refers to O'ertai, and it is even meant as praise.

Otherwise, Hu Zhongzao would not have forgotten Yeretai, and he would not have forgotten that they were also Tartars when he was corresponding with O'ertai and others every day.

As for the "Qing wind does not know words, why (must it) turn the books in disorder?" cited by a certain gentleman, it was written by Xu Jun, a Shujishi of the Yongzheng dynasty. "The Ming Dynasty will spread (periodically) its wings," "Fly to Qingdu in one fell swoop," "I see the Emperor of the Great Ming today (reunite again), let's put Hu'er aside for now," is from Xu Shuwei's *One-Pillar Building Poem*. They came before and after and have nothing to do with Hu Zhongzao. I don't know if this is a mistake on my father's part?

In fact, Hu Zhongzao had no ethnic prejudices at all, and Qianlong was clearly aware of this. The verses he extracted and the charges he made were very far-fetched, and it was clear at a glance that they were fabricated. Only the line "Remember the first gate of Xilin" was truly where Qianlong resented, and this was secretly in line with his repeated edicts prohibiting ministers from forming factions. Therefore, when Hu's case was concluded and reported, Qianlong's imperial decree dismissed ethnic entanglements and only spoke of sectarianism. In that part:

"Hu Zhongzao relied on his teacher's school and was willing to be a vicious dog. His poems mention slanderous tongues and blue flies, and according to his confession, they actually refer to Zhang Tingyu and Zhang Xi. It can be seen that his sectarianism is deeply rooted. Even Zhang Tingyu's use of people may not be without regarding O'ertai and Hu Zhongzao as outlaws. O'ertai and Zhang Tingyu were also unable to achieve great things because they met the Emperor Kao and me. Otherwise, what could not be done! When ministers stand in court, they should have the heart of serving the country with loyalty and dedication. If they all harbor opinions, then the petty people who rely on them will recklessly speculate and agree with each other, gradually becoming like fire and water. The evils of factionalism in ancient times all stemmed from this..."

Relying on his teacher's school and being willing to be a vicious dog is the true crime of Hu Zhongzao, and it is also the end of the road for the slaves I spoke of.

Many of the literary inquisitions of the Qing Dynasty had unspoken meanings. For example, Cha Siting's execution by Yongzheng was not because he came up with the topic "Where the people dwell," cutting off the head of the two words "Yongzheng," but because he was originally a former subordinate of Longkodo; Shen Deqian's execution by Qianlong was not because of the poem praising black peonies, "To seize red is not the correct color, different species are also called kings," but because he included poems that Qianlong replaced, tampered with, or ghostwrote in his own collection, exposing the charade. Hu Zhongzao's poetry case is just one such situation.

Peach Blossoms on the River 174

— Leng Mo

It was also such a cold spring, and it kept raining. It finally cleared up later, but the spring decreased in inverse proportion to the increase in sunny days. In idle talk, everyone regretted losing an opportunity to go for a spring outing. In Nanchang, everyone goes to Sancun to see peach blossoms every year in March, but by this time, the peach blossoms should have already faded. With the perspective of a foreigner, I argued that the peach blossoms would not fall so early. Although the production of sugarcane convinced me to admit that Nanchang's climate was earlier, I still勉强argued that this year's cold spring might produce different results. In fact, everyone originally hoped for such an excuse, but they used another reason to accompany me. I had long thought of taking a boat on the Gan River, but everyone thought this was an unheard-of absurd action and did not agree. Now, borrowing the excuse of seeing peach blossoms to take a boat ride was a suitable excuse, so we changed seeing peach blossoms to setting off for a river trip.

In order to have a longer water journey, we abandoned the usual pier for going to peach blossoms and instead went out of Tengwang Pavilion. There is no trace of Tengwang Pavilion, and the surrounding area has become a key area for loading and unloading goods. Assuming that those elegant scholars who lamented the sinking of ancient sites would rebuild Tengwang Pavilion, I wonder if they would be surprised to find that the scenery of "sunset glow and solitary wild ducks flying together, autumn water and the long sky sharing the same color" can never be seen again? Or would they close the building door and continue their dreamy dream of "reciting and chanting remotely, and unrestrainedly flying with inspiration"? We tried to think that in Wang Bo's time, he had to sigh, "The Orchid Pavilion is gone, and the Zize has become ruins." He didn't think that Yan Boyu's grand meeting had anything to cherish, so why should later generations cherish it for him? Looking at Baihuazhou, it has been completely renovated, but there is still no way to improve the pond water of Donghu. What is the point of all this?

Our budget for boarding the boat at Tengwang Pavilion failed unexpectedly. There wasn't a single boat there. The boats had all gone to the pier for seeing peach blossoms to catch business. So, we walked back along the river to that place. On the way, we saw many people returning with peach blossoms. We knew that this time's peach blossoms were set to be seen. At the pier, shouts were clamoring, "Go see peach blossoms, one dime per person to board the boat and it will leave immediately." We boarded the most convenient boat. We thought that since there were five of us in total, it would leave immediately. Unexpectedly, we had to wait until there were ten people. This boatman still didn't set sail but discussed with another boatman about transferring the passengers, with him collecting half of the fare. We knew we had been cheated. Paying a higher fare would have been fine, but we were really unwilling to be treated as commodities at the same time. Therefore, although the five people who came later were sold off and went to other boats, we stubbornly stayed on his boat, wanting him to ferry us himself. Who knew that our method was driving ourselves into an even deeper trap? We went from being commodities to advertisements. Our presence on the boat led later arrivals to misunderstand that the boat would leave soon and successively come up to become commodities. This method of exploitation really made us angry and helpless. We got off the boat to find another boat, but no one dared to agree to load us. We realized that this was meeting Zhang Shun on Xunyang River, but we still didn't believe that we were still in the Water Margin era. We returned to the original boat and negotiated with the boatman. Negotiation was really ineffective, but we, a total of five people, stood across his bow, cutting off the way for passengers to get on his boat, which made him realize the actual damage. Finally, he had to let us call the boat smoothly, and the fare was only five cents per person. For the time being, we were confident that we had overcome the difficulty. But it was really only temporary. After the boat had traveled a distance, the boatman told us that he was the one who was losing out, and we were still left with a sense of disappointment.

The boat was returning north, all the way to the mouth of Tengwang Pavilion, around the sandbar opposite the pavilion, and then turning into the inter-river and folding back south. There were also sparse households on the sandbar, and one of them was at the northernmost tip of the island. There were remnants of stone embankments on both sides of this island's corner, but they had been dilapidated and out of shape. I thought that there might have been a great building on this, so I asked my companions if it was Chao Wang Zhou—the Chao Wang Zhou where Tengwang Pavilion was originally located. My companions couldn't answer the name of the island but knew that Chao Wang Zhou was outside the inter-river. Then is there a river beyond Chao Wang Zhou? No one could answer, so there was no result. Even the location of the Sancun we were going to was never clarified. The boats for seeing flowers were all moored in one place, but after going ashore, we had to walk three or four miles along the river to see villages with scattered flowering trees. When asked for the place name, it was already Sancun, but when we moved forward and asked again, the villages along the way answered with the same name. It wasn't until we reached a village where there was no trace of tea stalls that we were told that it was already Liucun. According to the villagers, the best peach blossoms were actually in Qicun and Bacun. The words were probably somewhat credible, because some tourists were walking towards a more distant road, but we were walking on the way back, sitting down in a place that could be roughly considered Sancun.

In reality, no matter which section, there were more willows than peach blossoms. Whether on the edge of the fields, on the ponds, or on the graves, there was no lack of willow trees. Peach blossoms were all in people's yards. Peach trees are not more difficult to grow than willow trees. I don't know why people are unwilling to plant them everywhere, and I also don't know if those planted outside are not easy to preserve. People who see flowers are all happy to take some flowers back. If there are wildflowers to pick, they probably won't spend money to buy them. Flower prices are quite expensive, and few are broken off to sell to tourists. Most are just willow-woven flower baskets decorated with some flower petals. To buy whole branches of flowers, you must find a villager to break them off the tree temporarily, but tourists often refuse to sell a branch once they have decided on one. According to one companion's opinion, that branch can probably produce peaches with a far higher value, and it is not intended to raise the price. This idea was slightly confirmed from a tea stall old man. According to him, the business of peach blossoms was very good in previous years, and the income from selling tea in one season was more than ten yuan, and the flowers also sold for about ten yuan. Now the tea business is not good, so he hopes to find some compensation on the peaches. He doesn't think that the situation during the flowering season is bad, and the situation during the fruit season cannot be optimistic either.

There were still not few tourists this day. Although as a foreigner, I didn't feel much interest, my companions would also introduce conversations that used tourists as a topic. Among the tourists they recognized, some were women selling their youth. Seeing this while seeing peach blossoms naturally easily aroused associations, of course, eventually归入归入归入 the set of frivolous peach blossoms. So, they gradually and naturally talked about the end of spring and the withering of peach blossoms. Who is like the villagers who care about the peach tree's fruit? Most people are just waiting for the second spring.

Two Kinds of People 175

— Zi Gang

Shouldering a layer of dust and a sorrowful heart, I entered the platform.

The southbound Blue Steel train, scheduled to depart at 3:35, was already there, emitting white smoke and the smell of coal, its hissing and booming sounds stirring up the travelers’ anxiety and melancholy. The locomotive, as if a stomach, swallowed the towering clouds, making a strange cry that drove people mad.

The platform was packed with voices, countless footsteps jumping back and forth. Suitcases and packages were tucked under arms. The red-vested men were, at this moment, for bread—or should I say for hazelnut bread and corn buns?—panting. The policemen were pacing back and forth with measured steps.

Having savored enough of the taste of farewell, I also told a lie to brush off the inquiries of friends, and then slipped out of the ancient city alone with simple luggage, like a thief, without a sigh—no, perhaps the sigh was in my heart.

The loudspeaker was already broadcasting, its grand tune repeating over and over again, reporting in both foreign and domestic languages. People became more frantic, the clamor pervading the clouds.

With great difficulty, I squeezed into a third-class carriage. A lone traveler, I was stared at by some strange eyes: What's wrong, no friends to see you off?

Forgetting this, I circled around, looking for an empty seat.

I was almost disappointed. People had occupied a bench that could accommodate three or two people with their luggage. Those traveling long distances had spread out their blankets, stretching their legs, their leisurely expressions telling others: Spare your breath.

I put down my suitcase, preparing to stand until Tianjin. Surely, many passengers would get off there.

"Hey, there's space here!"

Startled by this seemingly familiar "Hey," a hand lightly patted my back from the left.

A sincere, unadorned face, warmth in its small eyes, a bald head still showing green, obviously newly shaved. A neat blue cloth gown covered a cotton robe. Comparing it to my own year-round blue overcoat, I couldn't help but blush. I turned sideways and greeted him.

The corners of his small eyes crinkled together, so shy. This was the unique loyalty of young people from the North, with a touch of rustic charm.

After learning that I was going to spend two nights on the train, this companion moved his bag to the seat opposite, muttered a few words to his companion in that seat, then turned back to me:

"Sit here. Two nights on the train is tough. This bench is just enough to sleep on. We're going to Dezhou, getting off at midnight." His Shandong accent pronounced "De" as "Dei." I felt a sense of familiarity. I rarely heard the Shandong accent.

"You should sit next to me; I don't need to lie down yet." I caught a glimpse of his companion's disgusted look. He disliked the young man meddling, forcing him to bend his outstretched legs.

However, the young man shook his head, as if unaccustomed to sitting on a bench with a girl, and lowered his head, twisting a white canvas money bag, playing with the string, circling it around his fingers.

"This is a shop assistant who spends all year behind the counter," I guessed.

Their conversation confirmed my guess.

His companion lit a cigar.

He was a shrewd old hand in business. Even though it was early February, with its initial warm weather, he was still wearing a fur coat over a leather jacket. As the carriage gradually warmed up, the portly merchant took off his outer coat. The young companion was pulled at the sleeve, but he indifferently allowed him to fold it, as if straightening it out.

"Are you in a hurry to get home after you get to Dezhou?" Sitting down, the portly merchant started chatting, apparently they had just gotten acquainted.

Mentioning home, the young man licked his lower lip, squinting his small eyes: "There's still fifty li to go, by animal."

"Isn't there a bus? Much faster!"

"Much faster, um," his eyes dodging the smoke rings from the portly man's mouth, "but it costs four or five mao. Hiring an animal, one baozi is more than enough. (Note: One bao gan'r is one hundred coins, about two mao according to the Northern market price.)"

As if unwilling to be met with the portly man's coldness, the young man continued enthusiastically:

"Another thing is, the bus has a set schedule, and you have to eat a meal while waiting. With a donkey, you can go anytime, saving you from going to a restaurant. That saves another four or five mao. Sigh, it's been four years since I ate a meal at home—"

Melancholy and the anticipation of the joy about to come collided in the young man's heart, and for a moment, he couldn't go on, smiling as he licked his lower lip.

"Ah, four years! I go back and forth once a month to handle goods. It's really hard work for a little bit of stinky money, so I just have to 'zheteng' (Peking slang, meaning to travel back and forth). But recently, the tea business has been okay. No matter how poor people are, they'll still drink tea—" He couldn't help but shake his bent right leg with pride. The young man's back immediately got a mud stain, but he didn't care and reached back to brush it off, continuing the topic:

"You must be making one or two wan a year? Our sundries shop made nearly a wan last year, but, what does it have to do with us xiao ji huo ji (shop assistants)..." The lean face turned red. This time, licking his lower lip evoked boundless indignation. "At best, we get ten or eight yuan at the end of the year. There's no hope."

"Take it slowly. I started with just a thousand yuan. How much salary do you get? Have you finished your apprenticeship yet?"

"I just finished last year. I only get—" The bald head slightly shook: "Six silver dollars a month! There's no way without capital. The family has had floods for years, and can't grow watermelons well. 'The family' still needs me to give them some money." -- Speaking of women, the young man felt shy, perhaps because it was a semi-estranged new bride after four years of separation.

Darkness fell. Past Tianjin, the calls of meat buns filled the windows. The lean face picked up a pile of buns, offering them to his companion. Although the portly man had already ordered a plate of egg fried rice, he accepted one out of politeness, saying he didn't have any change, pulling out a wad of banknotes from his short coat pocket, then stuffing them back in.

The portly merchant ate his egg fried rice, sprinkled with ham, alone, with a contented expression:

"It still has some taste..."

The shouts of newspaper vendors interrupted his praise. Holding a newspaper toward the plate of egg fried rice, the portly man nodded, tapping the waist of the blue cloth gown with his foot:

"Hey, excuse me, I don't have any change."

The young man carefully untied the tightly wound white canvas bag, gently paying ten copper coins.

As the lights came on, the carriage quieted down. Passengers abandoned the darkness outside the windows, falling asleep. The young man was a little tired, leaning on the back of his seat with his eyes closed, clutching his money bag and the handkerchief tied to his back containing his ticket. His simple face looked even warmer, that warmth covering up the habitual obedience and submission. He was dreaming, dreaming of home, dreaming of his wife and children, dreaming of exploitation and ruin…

Otherwise, why would he smile and frown by turns in his sleep? I didn't dare to move, afraid of waking him when a trace of joy floated on his brow. He still had to ride an animal home after getting off the train!

I don't know when the train stopped again. A sudden braking jolted me awake. The two men on the opposite seat had stood up. The lean one was helping the portly man stand up to take down his leather suitcase, wine bottle, and mirror frame... He himself only had a cloth bag and a rattan basket.

"Hey, I haven't paid for the egg fried rice yet. Do you have any change?"

The lean one hesitated, finally giving the portly man a satisfactory answer, unbuttoning his coat and taking out a small, tightly rolled package from his underwear. It was wrapped several times like a lotus leaf roll, inside were a few limited banknotes, neatly folded. He selected three single-corner bills from the middle.

The dish collector nodded, taking the money from the portly man.

"I'm sorry to use your money."

"Don't mention it, we're fellow countrymen, fellow countrymen!" The young man smiled gently.

I watched this companion get off the train, his shadow carrying the boxes disappearing into the midnight lights of the platform.

It's been a month, and that bald head and those narrow eyes are still haunting my mind. I hope life kicks away his obedience and his submission. Sheep can only be slaughtered.

The Coming Day 176

— Xi Jin

Let it transform into a thousand kinds of grotesque faces,

From deceit and tyranny, we grow.

No arrangements can deceive anyone;

Having lost our dreams, having lost our tears,

The suffocating climate should burst with a clap of thunder.

The coming day shall be our day,

The vigorous fire of anger warms our breasts, we must sing,

We cannot just suffer in sorrow and grief,

We must trample on all the new shackles of arrangements,

Struggle! Establish a brand new era.

Shattered Mood 177

— Qu Yi

When a person reaches a point where there are no ideals to pursue, the shattering of that mood can probably be compared to an exploding light bulb—the light before one’s eyes disappears, and in the darkness, only fragments remain that trip one up.

This makes me always remember what happened that afternoon.

Because I couldn’t find a friend I was visiting, Lao Tian and I were idly wandering around the Dapu Bridge area. After crossing the bridgehead, we both wanted to drink a few cups of wine to dilute the boredom in our hearts. So we found a wine shop on Lixie Road.

The wine shop had a two-bay facade. On the right was a corner-shaped counter, facing the street. On the left, against the wall, were stacked some wine jars, all of them old earthen jars covered in mud, as if they had just been taken out of a cellar, immediately reminding people of the taste of aged Shaoxing wine. Right at the part facing the steps, there was a small table with inscriptions, and someone was sitting there, engraving words with his head down.

We sat down at a table near the counter.

The owner, using a very scientific method, hammered a copper tube into the muddy head of the jar to draw the wine from the jar, but when he brought this yellow wine, there was still a drowned fly floating in it.

We drank wine, peeled peanuts, and chatted about everything. Life was boring. The past footsteps had nothing to commemorate. We had no plans for the future. We talked about the present, the present moment; we silently lowered our heads to the rim of the wine glass, reflecting our faces. Whenever we looked at each other, dry, bitter smiles would float on the corners of our mouths. The wine slowly dried up too!

Just as we were about to order another jin of Shaoxing wine, a Russian soldier sauntered over from the street. One can always imagine his appearance. Dry, bitter yellow hair like horse mane, a bloated, reddish-brown face, a suit of black, tattered clothes invariably covered in grease or mud and dust, and, as usual, dragging a pair of Chaplin-style worn-out leather shoes—this loyal soldier who, to commemorate the hell he himself created, refused to enter the heaven built for them by others, finally limped over here. He stood in front of the counter facing the street, and, for the sake of survival, abandoned his due aristocratic language and used the Shanghai language of the colonial world market, pointing to a black wine jar on the counter, saying:

“That one—one hundred coins!”

So he fished out a handful of copper coins mixed with dust from his suit pocket, like panning for gold, looking around the room extremely seriously with his blue eyes.

The owner, with extreme familiarity, poured him two cups of white spirits, just like he would serve the coolie boatmen on this road. I turned to Lao Tian and said:

"Maybe he's a general?"

Lao Tian nodded and took a drink. —However, he remained silent.

"Russian soldier! Russian soldier!" Suddenly, a call came from the left. I turned my head and saw that the inscription craftsman, who seemed to be held down by someone's large palm and could never lift his head again, this time, with a vengeful mood, had smile lines like crucian carp tails dragging out from the corners of his eyes, greeting this soldier, who might have been born a general.

"What is it?" He took the wine from the counter, drank it cup by cup as if drinking plain water without even frowning, then spat some saliva and said:

"Let's compare! Let's compare!" The craftsman said, suddenly laughing out loud.

"Okay! Compare! Compare!" He said, unbuttoning his suit trousers, pulling out a small thing that they originally wanted to use to maintain the aristocratic bloodline but was now aimless and dejected. He held it in one hand, shaking it up and down: the other hand pointed at the craftsman for a moment, then at the thing, as if venting some deficiency, cursing: "Niang mai min de! —Okay! Let's compare! Niang mai min de!"

So the proprietress and the craftsman both burst into laughter; but I, as if drenched in cold water, watched Lao Tian's lost face in the midst of the smoke and alcohol tasting of life.

"Niang mai min de! Niang mai bi de!" He kept mumbling, spitting out boring saliva, slowly locking up his trousers, hobbling away. But the victorious laughter in the shop continued for a long time, like cracked bamboo strips.

Looking at his receding figure, I thought: This kind of hero who seems to find satisfaction in being mocked by others, does anyone still remember the historical fact that he once squandered the sweat and blood of others for his own lewd pleasure? Does anyone still remember the age-old feats of using whips and bullets to play with other people's lives, obliterating the existence of others with his own laughter and joy? —However, in such a great era, as a small person, wading through the streets, spinning like dust in the wake of footsteps, showing his own powerlessness and weakness everywhere, then, perhaps there is a shadow of ourselves on him!

The Tragedy of Overseas Chinese 178

— Li Wen

The term "Overseas Chinese" has always been associated with the gleam of gold in the eyes of most people. Some people only see a few "successful" "Overseas Chinese magnates" who have returned to the country with large sums of gold and silver, displaying extraordinary pomp. As a result, donations, efforts to revitalize industry for the motherland, and even a whole host of praises such as "blessings of the motherland," shower down on these wealthy Overseas Chinese like raindrops. In the eyes of some people, wealthy Overseas Chinese have become a benevolent deity of wealth who relieves suffering and rescues people. Money is instantly exchanged for endless "worship." But beyond these very few wealthy Overseas Chinese, there are many more poor Overseas Chinese. The poverty, pain, and miserable oppression suffered by these poor Overseas Chinese are difficult to find even the faintest impression of in the eyes of those who only worship wealthy Overseas Chinese. The cries of suffering from the majority of oppressed Overseas Chinese have never shaken the eardrums of those in the motherland who only know how to worship wealthy Overseas Chinese. In fact, most of the wealthy Overseas Chinese who have already "succeeded" can be said to have struggled through countless difficulties and hardships to achieve their current status. When they were still deeply mired in the abyss of poverty and pain, no one paid any attention to them either. But when they "succeeded," in the eyes of the people of the motherland, their entire lives changed instantly. They instantly transformed from a position of poverty and helplessness into idols worshipped by all. This is because the gleam of gold has emanated from them.

These past few days, this newspaper has been running a serial report about the tragic plight of poor Overseas Chinese from the Fujian and Guangdong areas who have returned to the country, been deceived into being transported back to the Nanyang region, and then forced to return to the country again. These poor Overseas Chinese were originally overseas, but in recent years, due to the economic collapse in the Nanyang region and the increasing oppression from the local imperialist governments, they were unable to make a living and had to be forced to return to the country one after another. However, the rural areas of the country are becoming increasingly dilapidated, and there is no place to stand either. As a result, some people in the shipping companies in the Fujian and Guangdong areas came up with the absurd idea of ​​deceiving them, saying that the Nanyang economy had improved day by day, and that the local government's treatment of Overseas Chinese had also been greatly improved, which was a great opportunity to go there again. They believed this to be true, and pawned their belongings and borrowed money, barely managing to scrape together enough travel expenses and handing them over to the shipping companies to be "transported." They hid in the bottom of the triple-layered cabins, packed together with the cargo. Some were suffocated to death in transit, and were thrown into the sea when the ship returned to Hong Kong. When they arrived in Nanyang, they were discovered by the local government, all detained, and expelled back to the country. At this time, they had run out of money and were truly "with no way to go to heaven or earth." There are still four or five hundred of them stranded in Nanyang, unable to advance or retreat. This is what the newspaper reported. They, like the wealthy Overseas Chinese worshipped by some in the motherland, are also so-called "Overseas Chinese," but the results they obtain are so opposite. At this moment, who among those who worship wealthy Overseas Chinese has the time to pay attention to these poor Overseas Chinese who cannot advance or retreat!

Grandfather 179

— Tian Qi

Grandfather was a talented craftsman and sculptor. But the fate of his life was arranged under the gears of poverty. The peace and happiness of the world never fell upon him; In difficult days, biting hard on teeth, shouldering the burden of life, sighing and hoping: watching the spring come and spring go, flowers bloom and flowers fall. National sweat flows out, blood is squeezed dry, time gave him a cruel judgement, he is old! He can no longer squeeze his sweat and blood from an aging body for life to suck, in this lonely declining twilight years, he only gets to bring a sad mood, every day, quietly lying on a small table, finely carving and polishing his genius, seeking a little spiritual comfort.

The house is always so cold, empty, never revealing a voice of happy laughter, or casual conversation. Every day, from sunrise to sunset, grandfather himself hunches over, walking in and out, his wrinkled and dull face is always covered with a layer of gloomy look, sitting down, without saying a word, putting on his reading glasses, the knife in his hand gnawing at a gnarled piece of wood, tick-tick-tick, like a little mouse biting on hard food, making a fine rustling sound. Finally, he softly sighs, looks up and stares for a while at the two children squatting on the eaves digging mud and sand, and then gets up and searches in a bamboo basket hanging on the wall for two pieces of cake, calling kindly. "Come, Ah Ying and Ah Zha, watch the door, Gong Gong (grandfather) will be right back." My sister and I both smiled with satisfaction.

Grandmother walked into the room, saw the table full of knives and saws, wood and sawdust, and often nagged and ridiculed grandfather. Sometimes grandfather couldn't bear it and angrily retorted to grandmother. "What do you know!" Then he was silent again, then put down the knife in his hand and turned his face to grandmother, and the two of them talked about household matters, calculating uncertainly when the Nanyang water passengers would arrive, and perhaps uncle would send money. At this time, I always felt that something bad was going to happen in the house, and I didn't dare to look at the bamboo basket hanging on the wall, so I quietly pulled on my sister's sleeve and slipped out the door.

Year after year, time is long and endless, grandfather's back seemed to hunch over even more, and the long beard under his chin became longer and whiter. At the same time, there were several more very exquisite small ornaments on his small table, and grandmother's ridicule came even more often. However, grandfather did not seem to be satisfied with this, and every day he still lay on the small table from sunrise to sunset, silently carving and polishing, whiling away his lonely days, he seemed to be able to get comfort in his heart and spiritual sustenance only by constantly creating and working without interruption.

One day, grandfather finished a fruit platter for sacrifice, the finely carved flowers, the beautifully dazzling gold-leaf patterns, and the bright vermilion lacquer, all harmoniously and skillfully constituted the exquisite and delicate, elegant and refined appearance of this fruit platter. Grandfather was truly satisfied, he felt that he had gained supreme glory, and that all the past labor and energy spent had been fully rewarded. He let his knives and saws rest for several days.

One day, grandfather suddenly took this dish box out, but when he came back, the dish box was not brought back. He just looked very depressed, took out two long packets of silver coins from his sleeve, sat down by the table and stared blankly. That day, my sister and I did not get to eat his cakes. From that day on, grandfather was silently lying at the table again, finely carving and polishing…………

Shepherd Old Man 180

— Fang Zhou

He has lived at the foot of this mountain slope for more than fifty years, and in these fifty years, he has lived a solitary life relying solely on herding sheep. He is like that kind of old man in the poems of ordinary people and in the paintings of painters, existing lonely at the foot of this mountain slope: from youth to adulthood, from adulthood to old age, he has never left that mountain slope, nor has he done any other business, always herding sheep in this mountain. Every day he stumbles up the mountain slope, stopping beside a cluster of large elm trees, and the lambs scatter, searching for their needed food in the gray-yellow pile of withered grass. He himself runs to a high place and sits on a broken tablet in front of a grave, leisurely smoking his dry tobacco pipe.

The Chicken Cage Mountain in the early morning is hidden in a thick morning mist, the sky is gloomy and somewhat hateful, and the heavy air permeates the solidified silence, making people feel oppressed even when breathing. The gray and dim clouds are pasted even tighter, and the weather is colder than when he got up, and the pine waves in the mountain are already surging; he is wearing that stiff and broken blue cloth coat, and he really can't stand it. He sits there shivering, two clear streams of snot crawling on his gray-yellow beard, he moves away his dry tobacco pipe, raises his trembling hand, wipes his mouth with his sleeve, and then exhales a puff of smoke:

"It's going to snow again!" He supports himself on the ground with that three-foot-long dry tobacco pipe, which also serves as a sheep herding bamboo pole and a crutch, and stands up, gazing at the sky, saying as if sighing.

He is most afraid of encountering snowy and rainy days, because in these weathers he cannot let the sheep out, but keeping them locked up for a day requires a load of dried mulberry leaves.

The sheep are his companions and his life. In the past, at the most, he alone had herded

Page 18

two hundred ewes, grazing them around Chicken Cage Mountain during the day. Sometimes he would even pull open his sandy throat and hum a pastoral song, and he had to cut two bundles of dried grass every day. Because at that time wool could be sold for a dime or several cents per pound, shearing and sheepskins were very valuable, so he lived a very stable life. Although lonely and hard-working, he only worked mechanically and lived mechanically. He settled in that ordinary environment, passing the days day by day without longing or sorrow. But now, he feels that one hundred sheep are not enough, and besides, wool sheep are not worth much these days, six or seven cents per pound and no one wants to buy them, and sheepskins and shearing are also very cheap; therefore, his life has changed from stable to unstable.

He drove the sheep up the mountainside, still letting them find food for themselves, but he hid in a wind-sheltered rock to smoke. He took puff after puff, spitting the light blue embers in front of him, letting the wind blow them away. He seemed to want to use the power of this smoke to warm his stomach and his whole body. Looking at the sheep, one by one wandering in the woods, in the withered grass, their bleating sounds were scattered around the mountainside.

A series of cockcrows came from afar, and he knew it was almost noon, so he reached into his chest and pulled out a few dry pancakes; but although the pancakes were hard, because they were nestled in his chest, they were still a little warm, and the aroma of that kind of buckwheat noodles drilled temptingly into his nostrils. He picked up a pancake and put it into his mouth, which was devoid of front teeth, and chewed it carefully, chewing it. But after barely eating two, his gums were already hurting so much that he couldn't bite anymore.

The lambs leaped and bleated very lively on the mountainside. He squinted his old, blurred eyes and looked at the eighty or so sheep; he thought: more than half of these sheep are pregnant ewes, but those rams have to be sold, otherwise no one will want them when spring comes.

It is already the time of winter's end and spring's return, but he hasn't sold a single one of his thirty or forty rams, yet the lambs are about to be born.

Shepherd Girl 181

— Zhu Kang

The shepherd girl, Baidanuolejin, lay prostrate on the grassland by the Satunke River, touching the small grass with her hand, and singing a Duerbote love song in a soft voice.

Above her head was the April sun, lazily scattering its coy smile. The Kexing'e Wuhang Plain was covered with a flat, boundless green felt, as quiet and stable as a sleeping girl, lying upside down in the gentle and warm sunlight. The purple flowers of the poplar trees sprayed fragrance, floating across the riverbank, gradually hiding in the air. The Satunke River, freed from its shackles, flowed leisurely, meandering south from the foothills of Mount Lusai Duan, edging the Kexing'e Wuhang Plain with an endless ribbon. The sky, the grassland, the river, the beach, ... the entire universe sparkled with bright, alluring colors, making this rough world tame and obedient.

The gurgling water broke the silence of the plain, and the herds of livestock in the distance and nearby, scattered like variegated stones on the grass; the tender and delicate green grass was painted with various colored spots, like a gorgeous carpet in a palace. The sheep playfully touched their horns. The lazy and stupid old cows lay basking in the sun on the grass, closing their eyes and snorting from time to time. A gunshot in the distant mountains startled the horses, which pricked up their ears. The light, thin clouds on the summit of Mount Lusai Duan also floated happily.

Baidanuolejin was drowsy from being caressed by the sunlight, her eyelids were dry and her body was so tired that she was about to become paralyzed. The singing had stopped in her mouth long ago. She slowly got up, rubbed her eyes, and stared blankly at Mount Lusai Duan. The old yellow dog beside her wagged its tail, its eyes looking straight at its master's expression. Baidanuolejin was obviously fantasizing about something? Finally, she ran around the flock of sheep in a circle, then ran back, leaned against the trunk of a poplar tree, and pondered foolishly: sometimes her brows furrowed, sometimes her face was full of smiles, this was naturally the memories of the past provoking her thoughts. (To be continued)

Nonsense 182

— (Blowing)

National News Agency Electric report from St. John, California, USA, a large group of swallows flew to this place again today. For sixty-eight years, the date of arrival of the swallows has been unerringly accurate, always flying here on March 19th and flying away on October 23rd. Even in leap years, they are never mistaken. Mr. Tan Lao said, presumably the swallows also have a calendar, so their coming and going is so accurate. March 19th can be called "Swallow Arrival" Day, and October 23rd can be called "Swallow Departure" Day. All those who violate the New Life Movement and do not observe time, please look at the swallows.

The loss from the floods in the United States is now estimated to be no less than 500 million yuan. Washington seems to be able to escape danger as the water level of the Potomac River has slightly receded, but preventive measures have not been relaxed in the slightest. The White House is surrounded by sandbags, and the scene is very unusual. Mr. Tan Lao said, although the United States is called a gold dollar country, if we Chinese use astrology to predict, we would definitely say that having wealth and water is very auspicious.

Nora (15) 186

— Wan Chao Chen Illustration Xin Xin Explanation

Nora, frightened and confused, heard the doorbell and mustered her spirits to open the door.

It was Dr. Nan Hai who came in.

Nan Hai painfully told her that his life's account was about to go bankrupt. – He was afraid that he would be buried in the grave and rot in less than a month. – When he got the definite bad news, he would send Nora a card with a black cross on it.

Nora, with a pitying heart, asked him to look at her feet, maybe he would look at other places. In addition, she asked Hai for strong evidence that they were good friends, and asked him to do something very, very difficult. Nan Hai was very happy to hear this, and he couldn't help but say: "Nora, do you think that he is the only person in the world who is willing—willing to die for you? I love you like—"

While they were talking, the maid Ailan brought in Kolock's card and handed it to Nora, making her scream in surprise.

Nan Hai asked her why, she said: It's a new problem, you go to the room and stay away from Taofo, don't let him come out.

Nan Hai laughed when he heard what was going on, so that's what it was, don't worry, I won't let him escape.

Ballad Singing 187

Cai Xiaofang Mao's Family Book

Central and Western (1040) from 1:00 PM to 1:45 PM

Opening "Ode to the Red Cliff"

Romantic scholar in Huangzhou. Every day I enjoy myself by the river. On the 15th day of Renxu Xin's year. I talked with two or three close friends. I leisurely asked to board the Red Cliff boat. A young moon rises from the eastern mountain. Leaning on the railing and looking at the Dipper for years. Playing the strings as a board to sing to the bright moon. I frequently fill up the cup with Taibai. A clear song and a cup of wine. The guests harmonize with the sound of the flute, the rhythm is quiet. The guest is a Taoist priest from the West. The sound he blows is lingering. The harmony is leisurely and long. Like a woman weeping on a lonely boat. We can lament Cao Mengde of that year. Composing poems and waving his spears leisurely. He went down to Jiangling and broke through Jingzhou. Thousands of axes flowed smoothly. He was indeed a hero of his generation. I don't know where he is now. Thirty-six thousand days easily pass. How fortunate it is for life to be like a mayfly. But now I see through false fame and fortune. Talking about what is connected, I am also ashamed. Wash the cup and drink. Look at the date pits. The cups and plates are messy and not free. We pillow on each other and turn into a small boat.

Since the establishment of singing groups in the broadcasting circle, from the most prosperous period to the current decline, jealousy, abuse, and secret injuries have always been prevalent. However, when asked about the person being scolded or the person scolding themselves, they will be at a loss. Especially pitiful are those who "blindly follow others." So I think if we still want to raise our heads and want to regain the lost ground, we should have a grand alliance, and no longer ridicule, be jealous of, abuse, or secretly injure each other. Immediately form a sound organization and unite.

No Need for Nanjing to Call A Rebuttal to "Doesn't Know Hart" 190

— Anonymous

I received a letter from a reader named "Anonymous," who told me a story from five years ago and attached a piece of writing, which is published below. I seem to remember that five years ago, Miss Liang lived next to the Commercial Press on Baoshan Road, and Miss Liang also sat in a broken car owned by someone named Chen. Let's not talk about "old lovers," but "doesn't know" seems like a joke. Editor

"Hart ran to Nanjing to enter the Central Photography Studio because he couldn't stand in Shanghai."

But "Hart" was finally lifted up in "Warrior."

On the 24th of this newspaper, a half-naked small photo of him was published, with a note beside it: "The 'Warrior' of the Central Photography Studio will be released soon. Liang Weizhu's old lover 'Hart' is one of the protagonists..." Unexpectedly, Miss Liang called the next day to declare: "Doesn't know."

Let's not talk about "old lovers," but the question of knowing or "not knowing" is worth raising.

I remember that "Hart" knew Miss Liang, that was definitely the case. The introducer was originally a friend of both parties, someone named Chen. (At that time, Miss Liang was not as comfortable as she is now living in Qinyuan Village.) But now Mr. Chen is dead, and Miss Liang probably became a red dance star, so she easily "forgets," so she called to declare "doesn't know." And we who are "standing by as observers" couldn't help but come out to testify.

I hope Miss Liang thinks about things from five years ago?

Oriental Literature Creation Issue Published 193

The first issue of Oriental Literature, edited by Hou Feng and featuring the works of scholars studying in Japan and domestic writers, will be published today. It contains the works of Guo Moruo, Xu Xingzhi, Xin Ren, Dong Ping, Dai Pingwan, Lie Gongshe, Wang Yuwang, Zhang Xiangshan, Pu Feng, Ya Ping and others, totaling 150,000 words. It is printed in 16mo format with more than 140 pages and sells for 20 cents. The general distributor is the Xinzhong Bookstore in Tong'an Lane, Sanma Road, Shanghai.
